O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	 O you, very dear son, I have completed this book which is the culmination of the knowledge of medicine along with its practice, and I have brought it to an end through its explanations and clarifications.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	 And it has come to me in a vision that I should complete it for you with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	 And because the work of hands is lost in our region and has become foreign to everyone, thus the knowledge has perished and disappeared, and there remains nothing of it except for the small descriptions in the books of the ancients which the hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	 And from this come errors and vanities, and intentions are closed off, and knowledge is made distant.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	 And it seems to me that I wish to revive the ordinance of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and I will address together the forms of the cautery irons and other instruments of the work, along with their arrangement and preparation as needed.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	 And because in our time no good master of hands can be found, the art of medicine is abandoned.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	 And it is necessary for one who undertakes this to be knowledgeable in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so that he knows the judgment of the members, and their forms and conjunctions and separations, and has knowledge of the bones and nerves and muscles and the number of them, and their movement and resting, and the place from which they issue. ‌
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	 Et pour cela dit Hippocrate que le nom avec le nom est beaucoup, et avec l'œuvre est peu; et de même dans l'art de la main.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	 Nous vous disons dans l'introduction de ce livre que celui qui n'est pas conscient des choses dites auparavant, doit se garder de tomber en erreur et de nuire aux gens; ainsi j’ai souvent vu beaucoup de ceux qui s’impliquent dans cette science et qui abandonnent leur savoir et leur expérience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	 Car j'ai vu un fou médecin qui coupa l'abcès de scrofules au cou d'une femme, et coupa les artères du cou; par conséquent, une telle quantité de sang s'écoula qu'il la tua.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	 Et vit un autre médecin qui enlevait une pierre d'un homme d'âge, et la pierre était grande; elle emporta avec elle une partie de la vessie, et l'homme mourut après trois jours.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	 And I had already been called to remove it, and I saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and knew well that if one cut him, he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	 And I saw another doctor who took care of a duke from our land who had a broken leg and with the fracture there was an open wound; and the doctor, full of ignorance, pulled the fracture together on the wound with strong ligatures, and left no salve at all for the wound, and left it like this for one term; and he commanded that it should not be unbound; and it stayed like this until the leg was completely swollen and the foot, and it came to ruin.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	 I was called to come to him, and I hurried to come untie the leg; and when I heard it dislocated, he was at peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	 But the corruption had already spread through the limb, and I could not heal it; and the corruption did not stop spreading through the limb until the limb was completely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	 And I saw another physician who opened an encysted abscess and then inflamed it through the malevolence of his practice.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	 For chancre, when it is purged of melancholic humor, one should not touch it with iron unless it is in such a place that all the corruption can be entirely removed.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	 And therefore, dear son, it is necessary for you to know that manual work is divided into two parts: namely, work where there is danger in many situations; and I will show in each section of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	 For which reason it is necessary that you take care of yourself, so that the foolish physician cannot speak ill of you. Therefore, take up your arms courageously, and undertake your patients lightly and firmly, and use the best method so that by the grace of God you come to salvation and be praised; and leave behind dreadful diseases of serious illness; and remove your arms from what causes you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you can pass from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	 Galen said in some of his admonishments: "Do not take on a serious illness, lest you be called a foolish physician.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	 "I have composed this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	 The first chapter is about fire cautery and about cauterizing wounds with medicine, and this chapter is arranged from the head to the feet; and about the forms of instruments, and about the irons used for cauterization, and about everything necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	 The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and about cupping and wounds, and about extracting arrows, and similar things; and this chapter is arranged and the forms of the instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	 The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things; and it is arranged from the head to the feet, and about the forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	 As we remember the work, it is necessary that I speak about the quality of each temperament and its harmfulness.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	 I say that the qualities of aid and harm are the longest discourse and subtle science, and secret responses; and many of the wise have spoken about this and agreed upon it; and few of their words suffice me, for I fear lengthiness.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	 I say that fire cautery helps universally in every condition where there is matter, except for two conditions: namely, hot condition without matter, and dry condition without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	 In hot and dry condition together with matter, some discussed and said that fire is of great help there; and others said the opposite: that fire does not help against disease that comes from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	 For the nature of fire is hot and should not be used to cure heat disease by heat or dryness, and that person who says the opposite says that fire greatly helps against heat and dry disease in the human body.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	 Because when you examine the man's body and its moisture according to the fire complexion, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	 And I agree with this statement.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	 Because I have found it so by experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	 Nevertheless, one should not interfere with it except for those who have experienced it, and who know through long practice the chapter on cauterization, and the diversity of human complexions, and their dispositions and causes of illnesses, and the occurrences and passage of time; we do not fear other complexions, especially in cold and moist diseases. ︎
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	 And all the physicians gathered and agreed on the use of cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	 And know, son, that cautery with fire is among the secrets of healing, and of greater benefit than cautery with burning medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	 For fire is simple, and does not extend beyond the member that it burns, and does no harm to any other member if possible.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	 Burning medicines travel from one member to another, causing the affected member to have serious illnesses; and possibly killing the patient. The fire, because of its high quality and the goodness of its substance, does not do this unless there is excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	 And this I have found through experiment and the length of my service and study that I have put into the art, and it is based on the truth of things; and for this reason I excuse myself for the length of my speech, because I do not wish to deprive you of the secret that resides in fire, and the quality of the work, how it drives away diseases of the body, as the philosopher said in demonstrating; now receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	 And know, son, that they agreed upon the time when the cauteries should be made, and chose patients.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	 And I say that a cautery is suitable in all seasons, because the harm occurring is remedied by the help of the cautery; and likewise if the cautery is for necessary pains urgent and hasty so that they cannot await the time when greater harm comes to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	 And do not think of it as the foolish physicians do; for the disease that is healed by cautery has no return; and they say thus; but it is not as they believe, because cautery is nothing other than medicine which moves the complexion, and dries the humors which are the cause of the pain, and is more effective than medicine for its swiftness in action, and for the virtue of its work and power.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	 And it happens that the disease comes sometimes according to the complexion of the patient and the place of the illness and its power; and superfluities are gathered in him through the consumption of food and similar things, unless cauterizations are administered in the place where there is little superfluidity and moisture, such as tooth cauterizations for pain, and similar things, and such pain does not return; but this happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	 And many people do not understand why cautery is called the last resort of medicine, and this is true; but they do not believe that cautery is worth anything after medication, but their belief is false, and cautery is the last resort of medicine because when we administer ways of cures in some illness and they are not effective, then we administer the cautery, and it is effective.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	 Then it is clear that cautery is the last resort in medicine, not according to the intention of foolish physicians.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	 The ancients said that cautery with gold instruments is more effective than with iron, and they said this only because of the quality of gold and the height of its substance; but I say that this is not true, for I have proven it and found that it is true in some men; and cautery with gold is more effective than with iron, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	 However, when you heat a gold instrument, you do not know when it is hot enough by the color of the gold, and it cools down quickly; and if one heats it too much, then it burns in the fire; and thus there are many obstacles to this.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	 And for this reason, we use fire cautery which we have prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	 Now I have arranged this chapter from the head to the feet, so that it may be easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	 of olive oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	 This cautery is good for moisture and cold on the head, and it has two effects: it is done because of an illness called "soda," and because of many humors that descend from the head to the eyes, ears, due to excessive dreams and toothache and throat pain, and especially for all diseases that come from cold, such as paralysis, soda, apoplexy, and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	 The form of this cautery is that the patient be purged with a medicinal solution, cleansing the head for three or four days, according to what the virtues and nature and custom of the patient can bear; and then let the patient's head rest.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	 Then let him sit cross-legged between your hands, and place his hands on some cloth. After that, place the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his two eyes; where your two fingers meet, make an incision there and heat the cautery called "olivare", this is its form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And place it on the signified spot of ink, and make an incision while stretching your hand little by little in rotation; then lift your hand immediately, and inspect the spot if you see the bone I sol (small) piece; and if you do not see it, then repeat the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you; afterwards take a small cloth, and place soft cotton inside, and put it on the spot, and let it remain for three days; afterwards place a moistened linen with butter; and leave it on until the burn is healed; afterwards treat the wound with the ointment called "tetrafarmaçon", until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	 And the ancients said that when the wound remains open longer, it cleanses more; and for this reason, movement helps.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	 And some said that one should let the cautery burn until part of the bone is burnt, and then scrape off what is burnt from the bone, and it should be treated.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	 And others say that one should let the cautery burn until, and press so hard that it cuts through the bone as wide as a spindle that women put in their distaffs, so that the humors may come out; and one should let the wound remain open for a long time; afterwards, one should treat and sew it.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	 And these two methods of cautery do not seem to me to be entirely good, except in some men where there is a way to fear; and more it seems to me that I should leave it; for the head has been weakened by the continuous solutions of nature, as we testify in other members; and also when the patient's head is weak by nature, and the first appearance of cautery is safer and better for me, I use this work then safely together.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	 of the ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	 When chronic pain occurs throughout the head and lasts long, the patient should use herbs and pills called "coccia," and purgatives of the head, and oils and plasters; and if a cautery is done as we have said before, it does not work.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	 Take care if the patient's head is of strong nature and not too cold; then cauterize under that cautery a little, as we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	 Then make a cautery over each vein of the head up to the bone, as we have said before, and make a cautery in the place called "vessel"; and there is the place where cupping glasses are put; and lift your hand so that you do not see to the bone: the patient feels much more pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak of it elsewhere; and the cauteries on the veins must be finer than those used to cauterize the middle of the head, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	 of the cautery of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	 When sudden pain occurs in one part of the head, and the disease extends to the eye, and the eye is purged with purgative medicines, and other cures that I mentioned in the division of diseases have been done, but none of this helps: then you make cauteries in two manners, namely with hot irons and with fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	 The cautery with hot irons is done this way: take a clove of garlic and remove its skin and place the two cloves in the temples where the pain is, and then pierce the temple in such a manner that you can fit the clove of garlic under the skin; and when it has been placed, bind it well and leave it there for XII hours; and then unbind and draw out the clove of garlic, and let the wound remain thus for II days or III; then apply a compress soaked in butter as long as it can hold.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	 After the treatment of inflammation, ensure it is healed; and if you see this, apply some of the combustible medicines that I have written in the twelfth treatise on combustible medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	 The iron cautery is performed in this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	 Heat the cautery whose shape is as follows:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	 And it is called "clos" because the tip is made in the shape of a nail with a small cavity inside, and in the middle there is a tiny opening; place it on the painful spot, hold your hand steady and turn it lightly until half the thickness of the cautery is burnt; lift your hand so that the outer part does not burn, for it should come out with an abundant flow of blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	 After put cotton in vinegar water, and place it on the area for three days; then put dampened cotton in butter, and then treat the area with ointment until it is healed; and if you wish to cauterize this headache with the cautery called "cultellare," do so with the entire tip, and be careful not to cut the artery in this new headache.
de emigraine	 of a migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	 When you treat a migraine as we have said before in the divisions of diseases, and it does not improve, and you see that the previous cautery from medicine and iron is not helpful, then it is necessary to heat the cautery called "cultellare" until it is white; and immediately place it on the painful spot for a half-inch long line, and remove your hand once, and hold it so that you do not cut the artery and do not reach the bone; and beware of the jawbone that moves when chewing, and let the nerve only move and not cause spasms in the patient, and beware of blood loss from the artery when it is cut, for there is great fear in cutting, especially for those who are not knowledgeable and experienced; and leave the work halfway; but I will tell you how to stop bleeding when an artery is cut, and I will show you the place where it is necessary in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	 And if you see that this cautery is not beneficial for the illness, and the patient is enduring, cauterize him on the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it is healed; and if you see, administer the cautery that we have said in the chapter on the extraction of the artery, with the cautery that has two blades; and this cautery is better and more helpful than the other.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	 of the ear pain due to cold
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	 When ear pain comes from cold, and one has worked with solvent medicines and other cures that we have said in the division, and the pain does not move, then heat this cautery which is called "point," of which here is the form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After pricking all around the sick ear, or around both if the pain is in both, and you distance yourself slightly above the root of the ear after you have marked the place; and let there be ten points around each ear; afterward, treat the place until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	 Of the mouth's torment
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	 Torture that must be cured by cautery is only that which comes from phlegm, as we have said in the division of diseases; and do not perform cautery on those that come from dryness or from nerve pain.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	 When you treat this appearance of torment which comes from the phlegm of ulcers and purges of the head and throat, and it does not work, then it is necessary that you cauterize the patient with three cauteries: one at the root of the ear, another a little outside the temple, and the third at the meeting of the two lips; and place the cautery in the part that looks healthy, and make a cautery on top of the ear slightly below the horn of the head, and another on the temple as long as a thumb; and leave the cautery there until half the cheek is burnt; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And it is similar to the knife we mentioned before, but it is a little more subtle and the blade must be a little larger; after caring for the place as I have said before, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	 When apoplexy is chronic and you treat it as we have said, and there is no improvement, and the patient does not have a fever, then make four cauteries: two on the two horns of the head, one in the middle of the head, one in the place called "vasselz" as we have said before, and the last cautery on the mouth of the stomach; and treat it as we have said before.
de litargie	 of lead
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	 For this illness, it is necessary to give the patient large pears and pills that cleanse the brain; then wash the patient's head thoroughly, and place on the occiput the sinapi plaster as written in the treatise on plasters; and this is the manner of cautery: do it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	 If he is cured thus, it is good; and if not, let him make III cauteries in the middle of the head descending to the neck, and have between each cautery II of large ones; and cure as the others, and if you see something added, and the patient is enduring, let him make I cautery in the middle; and if needed, II more on the two corners, and cure until it is healed; and let the cautery be called "olivare," as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	 of the coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	 The head must be cleansed of hairs and what we have said before; then wash the patient's head, then make a cautery in the middle of the head and on each corner, and one behind, and three on the spine of the neck; and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient is enduring, and the disease is severe, make four cauteries on the spine of the back; and let it be until the most of the heart is burnt, and lift your hand; then cure until it is healed, and let the cautery be called "olivare" as we have said before.
de l’epilempsie	 Of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	 The epileptic should not use the cautery except for those who are phlegmatic, and it is first necessary to purify the brain with years and other treatments that we have mentioned in the division when the patient is large and able to take medication.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	 And if it is a child who cannot tolerate it, one gives him gargling and chewing to purify the brain often with good foods; afterwards, one shaves his head in the middle, and there one makes a cautery as we have said before, and a cautery on the bladder, and on each corner; and if the patient is strong and able, one makes cauteries as I have said for those who have paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and the neck, and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to the manner that I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	 If the patient is a child, perform the subtle cautery in this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	 When due to melancholy there are corrupt and excessive humours or thick phlegm, then use the cautery of thin needles as we have said for those with paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	 And if the superfluidity inclines towards melancholy and the patient's body is moist, then give them something to drink that will purify the brain, as was previously explained in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After washing the patient's head, make a poultice of well-prepared linen, like a circle, and place it on the head; let the patient sit quietly, and be held securely on all sides; then present the poultice, and moisten it with old ewe’s butter; heat it gently by the fire so that the two may bear it; after emptying the circle inside the head, let it cool; and do this for the patient once a week along with other good treatment until they are healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	 And if you see cauterizing the wound by making several points throughout the entire cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	 This method of cautery softens the brain equally; then place moistened cotton on butter and goose fat.
de l’awe des eulz	 from the movement of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	 When the movement first comes to the eyes by the signs I mentioned in the division, then begin and give the patient something to cleanse the head, and guard it from all moisture, and make him sweat in a bath several times on an empty stomach.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	 Afterwards, instruct him to shave his head, and make a cautery in the middle of the head, and make two cauteries on the two temples if the descent is in both eyes together, or one if the descent is in one; and cut all the veins and arteries that are beneath the brain, and let the cauteries be long according to the width of the temple; and guard against an excessive flow of blood, and if you see too much blood coming out, then staunch it with such power as you have. ︎
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	 Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des artères et a l’incision la cautèle comment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautère ou hâtreil desoz les II os derrière.
dou cors des larmes	 du corps des larmes
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	 When the tears from the eyes are old and habitual and are on the veins or near the arteries that appear at the top of the head; and it is seen that they come from cold phlegm, then he makes the cautery as I said in the beginning of the work descending to the eyes: one cautery in the middle of the head, two cauteries on the temples, two cauteries under the two bones; and if more is needed, he cauterizes wisely over the entire top of the head with a small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	 Of the body tears within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	 When you medicate it according to what we have said in the division, and it does not help at all, then give the patient to drink three nights of cochies; after that, shave his head, and make a cautery in the middle of the olivary cautery; and make two cauteries with the cautery called "clavilis" on the two eyebrows, one a little below the eyebrows; and beware of the artery so that you do not cut it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	 And this is the shape of the cautery which is called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	 When the papilla of the eye is softened by illness and moisture, then cauterize it with this cautery which is called "olivary".
de coi ci est li forme:	 de la raison pourquoi cela se produit :
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	 And if you see that it does II cauteries on the II sore places as long as the sores are; and do not leave the hand except until the third part of the paper is burnt, according to the manner that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	 of the hair that pricks the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	 Sometimes it happens that the hairs of the eyes are turned towards the inside and prick the eye, and then one does cauteries in two ways: that is to say with fire or with burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	 For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	 When they are born and equal, then place the patient in your healthy hand; afterwards make on the paper of the eyes a figure that is like the leaf of myrtle, and let the beginning of the sign be near the hairs; then put moistened cotton soaked in egg white and musk of peony on the eye, then heat the cautery which has this form:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Afterwards cauterize on the figure that you have signed little by little many times, so that the skin is burned in that place; and the sign of the health of the work is that you see the paper retracted, and the hairs raised to the tip of the eye; then lift your hand, and leave it like this for 3 days, then put moistened cotton in butter until the burn is gone; afterwards the cure of ointment until it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	 Et si après cela viennent les poils, et la peau est adoucie, alors recommence le cautère à cet endroit même, comme tu as fait précédemment; et si les poils sont absents, alors cautérise jusqu'à ce que la peau soit soulevée à sa place naturelle, qu'elle soit égale, et que les poils ne piquent pas l’œil.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	 The cautery of the burning medicine is that you instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even. Then make a form from parchment in the shape of the myrtle leaf; then take half a pound of French soap and one pound of vive chalz, and grind them together well. Do this quickly so it does not cool down, then spread it on the form you have made like the myrtle leaf, and place it on the skin of the eyes. And if the disease is in only one eye, you should work on that one; and if in both, do the same. Then put moistened cotton under the eye, with an egg white. And let the patient's head be in your hand and place your finger on the medicine, and press the poultice and the egg white every time the patient feels the biting of the medicine, for he will feel it as if by fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	 When you have done this for some time, remove the medicine with your finger.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	 And when the biting has passed, lift the skin away, and look if you see the flesh lifted as if it were raised by the constraint of fire or by incision; and if so, it is good.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If not, then put more medicine on the place where the medicine has not worked, until your work is equal and your eyes are set; then put on a cotton soaked in butter until the burnt skin falls off, after that cure the burn with ointment called "dyafenis" and others, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	 And if you must watch carefully your work with great care lest any of the medicine fall into the eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	 And if the skin becomes soft afterwards, and the hairs prick in the eye, then begin the treatment again on that place which is softened by the skin properly, as you have done before; after the cure until it is healed; and this is the shape of the leaf of myrtle:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	 And know that the eyes of men are diverse in size and smallness, and according to this should be your constrictions; and do not respond to the right way for he who has studied this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	 of the treatment of a fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	 When you treat a fistula as we have said in the division of diseases, and your treatments do not benefit, then it is necessary that you burn it with a cautery according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	 Command the patient to place their head in your hand; and let the attendant hold their head between your hands so that it does not move or lower its head; afterwards, put damp cotton on the eyebrow or on the juice of parsley on the eye; afterwards heat the cautery which is such: and it is shaped at the top like the tip of a feather, along with which is the cautery; if you wish, let it be pointed from one end to the other, and if you wish, let it be like a tent; but nevertheless, this one which is shaped is better for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	 Then press the fistula if it is open, and draw out the pus, and dry it; and if it is closed, work on it, and draw forth the vein; afterwards place a very hot cautery on it, and hold your hand to the cautery at the part of the nose above the eye, so that your hand does not shake; and put the cautery in the fat of the eye, and let it rot.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	 If you approach the beginning of the cautery up to the bone, it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	 If not, then begin the cautery again once more, and another if you need it, and leave it for three days; afterwards apply a moistened cotton in butter, and continue with the treatment of desiccating ointment until it is healed; and if forty days pass and it is not healed, then apply corrosive medicine until the bone is exposed; and the king according to what comes in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	 And there is a manner of cautery for fistulas that some ancients said.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	 Understand the fistula and open the place; afterwards put into the opening one subtle cautery of which the form is thus:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	 And they make in the quantity of an .З. of lead; and hold your hand firmly on the canthus, and let the patient not move at all, until the melted lead runs into his eye; and it is necessary to put on the patient's eye a moistened cotton ball with egg white or water: the lead thus acts on the site of the fistula, and cures by marvelous health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	 And if the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have spoken of, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	 If not, then a perforation must be made in the nostril, and the fistula should be brought back to the body of the nose according to its own proper place.
des crevaices en levres	 cracks in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	 Mouth ulcers often occur on the lips called "hair", and similarly on children's lips.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	 When you treat these ulcers as we have said in the divisions, and the treatment does not benefit, then heat a small cautery knife according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And quickly place it in those ulcers until it reaches the bottom; afterwards, treat the area with wax until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	 of the throat abscess
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	 When an abscess occurs at the root of the throat or in the uvula, or on the palate, or at the roots of the teeth, after it becomes putrid and rotten, and is healed, it turns into a fistula; and you treat it as we have said in divisions, and it does not benefit: then it is necessary that you have a cautery according to the size of the fistula; afterwards, open or pierce the opening of the fistula, and hold your hand so that the hot iron reaches the bottom and the place behind; and do this once or twice, afterwards treat it as we have said in treatments, until it is healed; and if it is treated thus, it is good; and if not, then you must expose the area and remove the infected bone, according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	 of the teeth's movement
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	 When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat them with medicines and it does not work, then put the patient's head in your lap; afterward, heat the cautery as shown here in this manner that you place a reed on the tooth; and quickly insert the hot cautery inside, and hold your hand so that the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth; after that, lift your hand and start the cautery again according to your will; after that, let the patient rinse their mouth with salt water, and keep it for an hour and spit out.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	 And in this way the tooth that was moving is made firm, and the softened gum is restrained, and the moisture causing corruption is dried up.
de la dolor des dens	 of toothache
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	 When toothache comes from cold, or there is cold in the mouth, and medicinal treatments do not help, then it is necessary to use cautery in two ways: cautery with butter and cautery with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	 Cautery with butter is done as follows: take butter from a cow and the end of an iron or bronze spoon; then take cotton and wrap it around the tip of a tent stake, wetting it in boiled butter, and place it quickly on the aching tooth, holding it until it cools; and do this often so that its virtue reaches the root of the tooth. If you see wool and cotton moistened with cold butter, and place it on the aching tooth, and put hot iron on top so that the heat reaches to the end of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	 The cautery with fire is such that you take a tube of iron or brass, and it should be thick enough that the heat does not reach the mouth of the patient; then heat the cautery, from which the shape will come afterwards, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery cools; do this often, for the pain will be removed that same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	 And it is necessary that the patient fills his mouth with good butter during this cautery, and then rinses vigorously; and this is the shape of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	 And make a cautery on whatever head you wish, according to what you have the power to do; and this is the shape of the tube:
des scrophules	 of the scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When the scrofula are from cold and moist phlegm, and do not respond to digestion by medicines, then heat the cautery head as follows: it should have two openings for the smoke to exit at the cautery of the other part; and place the hot cautery on the abscess once, or twice if necessary, until it reaches the bottom of the abscess. And if the abscess is small, place the cautery according to the size of the abscess, and leave it thus for three days; and put moistened cotton with butter on it until the burn is gone; after that, cure the place with onion and tentes until it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	 The shape of the dog:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	 When moisture prevails over the passages of the brain, especially when it comes from cold humors, then it is necessary that the patient be first purged with purgative medicines; afterwards make a cautery at the root of the throat, and take care not to go as far as the throat, and only burn for a short time.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Afterwards make another cautery at the juncture of the neck with the top of the spine, and let this cautery be called a "clavicle," as we have described its form before; and treat the place as we have said before until it is healed.
de la toust	 from the heat
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	 When the patient and the brain disease are of cold moisture, and the patient does not have fever or heat, and the disease is chronic, make two cauteries on the forehead in close places; and another cautery in the chest between the two breasts; and let this cautery be called a "clavicle" according to the form that has been said before.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	 And if you see, perform cautery by pricking all the cautery that is called "point" which forms as mentioned before in the disease of the ears; and let the points be up to XXX, or approximately thereof.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	 After curing the place according to what was said before, and let the cautery be at three times according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	 And because the cauteries are lighter, therefore you make three in succession.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	 Of the shoulder dislocation
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	 When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	 Afterwards, instruct the patient to lie on his back and side; afterwards, lift the skin which is inside the tickling with the fingers of your left hand; and if the joint is dislocated within, then heat the cauterizer which has two nerves thus is its form.
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	 and cauterize the skin until it pierces to the side, and comes with it four cauterizers; and because of this, cautery is done with the three-nerve cauterizer, so that the figures of cauterization are these six cauterizers; and the nerves are according to the delicacy of a tent, and this is the form of the three-nerve cauterizer:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	 And sometimes it is placed on this one nerve, so that there are eight cauterizers.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	 After place the cautery on the burn wound mixed with oil; afterwards make the patient rest, and let the limb not be moved for a long time until it is well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	 And if it is dislocated on top, which happens rarely, then make a cautery above the thick part of the burn, or many cauteries in pricking.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	 Because the joint is closed, and the moisture is removed, and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	 When cold and much moisture come into the stomach to such an extent that it strains his complexion, and many catarrhs befall him, and in the usual ways of treatment he does not benefit, then the patient must be placed on his back, and stretch out his legs and hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	 This is the line-by-line translation of the given Old French text into English:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	 And if you see to cauterize with a large cautery in the stomach according to this form; and he who has fear of this cautery, cauterize by pricking and marking on the stomach here, one point according to the amount that you wish; then cauterize with all the cautery which is called "point".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 After the treatment of the wound that we have had before, until it heals.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	 As for the liver, when pain comes from cold and moisture and great flatulence, such that it is put out of its natural complexion by superfluities; and the patient is treated with what we have said in divisions, and it does not benefit him at all, then the patient must be bled on his back; and mark three cauteries according to this form and this figure and this amount on the liver, below the hypochondriac region, where the rib of the man comes; and let there be between each cautery the thickness of a finger; and let the cauteries be long along the body, and do not press too hard with your whole hand on all the cautery; and let only half the head be burnt, and let the patient be upright on his feet; and if he cannot, then let him lie down, and stretch out his legs, and raise his arms; and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	 And if your intention is to cauterize these cauteries of the scalpel, if you are skillful and knowledgeable in the art, be careful not to burn the entire heart, for you would dry out the whole body; and do not go all the way to the boil, for the heart is very delicate in that place, and know this well.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	 When there is an abscess in the liver, and you want to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the membrane: if it is in the flesh, the patient does not feel pain too intensely; and if it is in the membrane, he feels intense pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	 And then, when this cure should be done by the physicians, it is necessary that the patient be placed on his back; and then place a cloth over the place where the abscess is, and then heat the cautery which is similar to a ray, as described here.
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	 And cauterize with the caustic until the heart is burned, and it reaches up to the sphincter, so that the protrusion is completely removed; after the care according to the care of the ulcers until he is healthy; and it should not be used by anyone for this cautery except those who have studied medicine for a long time, and through whom fewer diseases have run their course.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	 Then he can boldly work, nevertheless it seems to me that it is better to leave him.
dou cautere de pleuresin	 of the cautery of pleurisy
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	 The ancients said that for pleurisy one should make cauteries with the root of aristolochia, and in this manner: take a long root of aristolochia, the longest you can find, and let it be dry, as thick and as long as your fingers; and moisten it in oil, and hold it over the fire, and cauterize I cautery between the collarbone and the neck, and II small cauteries a little below in the part that is below the beard; and II cauteries between the fifth rib and the sixth, leaning slightly back; and I cautery in the chest, and I other on the stomach, and I between the two shoulders, and II on the sides of the chest outside the cautery that is between the shoulders; and do not press with your hand, but make it openly as if smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	 And they say that some old ones use the fire cautery in the form of a razor, and heat it and place it between the ribs until it reaches that abscess; and if the pain is severe, as we have said, concerning the liver abscess.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	 But in this work there is danger that the patient may die now or a fistula may occur which cannot be healed.
de la mice	 of the urine
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	 When you treat the disease of urine according to what we have said in the sections on treatments, and it does not benefit, then there are three ways of fire cautery which are all good.
