des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	 from the incision near the temple to the second incision; and scrape off all the skin that is between the two incisions up to the hairline above the bone, then make another part from the middle incision to the other second incision, and then remove this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	 If you insert into the first incision the instrument called "scalpel," which is very sharp on one side and soft, not sharp, on the other, it is this form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	 And place the sharp side towards the flesh to the heart, and the soft side towards the bone, and insert it until it reaches the middle of the incision.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes so that the incision is continuous until it reaches the heart, and then do another part in the middle incision until the other defect; and then draw out the blood equally, and press the place for the taken blood; then put into each incision a tent of old cotton, and put on dampened cloths in wine and oil and ashes, and guard that abscesses like these do not come there; and on the third day remove the ligature, and apply a large quantity of boiling water, then a dressing with basilicon ointment with rose oil, and other dressings with which one treats wounds, until it is healed. 😊
dou reume des eulz	 Of the moisture of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	 When someone comes with a sharp cataract, and you see the eyes thin and small, and weakening the sight, and the eyelids burnt; and the hair falls out, and there is pain in the head, and the patient sneezes; then know by these signs that those matters and this cataract do not come from anything but many veins, and the cure is as follows:
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	 And it is that you command the patient to shave his forehead, then make a great incision in the middle of the forehead, and another on both temples.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	 And begin from the incision of the left temple to the right, and let the cut be down to the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move while eating; and when the bone is exposed, wipe all the blood with a sponge, then insert old cotton and linen between the two lips of the incision; then bind over it with cloths moistened in wine and oil, and beware of hot abscess; when it is removed, you must rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then treat it with drying agents that make the flesh appear.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	 In such a manner: take two parts of wheat flower and four parts of colophony, and make an ointment; and administer it in these wounds to heal flesh completely.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	 Of the stoppage of ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	 All that falls into the ears is one of these four things: grains, animals, stones like ore, or seeds such as peas, beans; or liquid things such as water and oil and similar substances.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	 When it falls into the ear, stone or other kind of thing that does not fit in the ear and does not grow in the ear, put the ear in the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	 If you see the stone, then drip some drops of violet oil or sesame oil into the ear; and make him sneeze by appropriate means, and close his nostrils when the sneezing comes, and put pieces of cloth or wool around the ear; and then hold the ear up.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	 Much of the time this cure causes fever; and if it does not cause fever, then administer extraction with subtle pinchers, of which here is the form.
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	 If it causes fever with pinchers, that is good; if not, then administer extraction with a subtle lancet of fine edge; and if it does not cause fever this way, make a tube of iron and insert the end of the tube into the ear canal strongly, and stop up what surrounds the tube with soft wax so that the wind cannot enter with the tube; then draw out the fever strongly, for often it comes from this as we have said; and if it does not come out in such a manner, take juice of cowbane, which birds use, and put some in a suitable instrument for this purpose, and put a little cotton around it; then press the juice onto the stone or whatever it is, and draw out the fever.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if she does not heal from all these things that we have said, then hurry to cut the ear before an abscess and spasm come, and the manner of the cutting is this: first make the patient sit in a cephalic position, and extract blood according to the measure of its virtue, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small cut at the root of the ear in the fatty tissue or nearby area; and let the cut be like a moon, until you reach the stone, then remove it according to your ability, and suck it hastily into your mouth; and treat until he is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	 Et s’il s’agit de grains (abcès) à l'intérieur qui enflent, administrez une extraction. Et s’ils ne peuvent pas sortir, administrez un cataplasme fin et subtil selon cette méthode :
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	 and make an incision in that abscess
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	 But do not do this when you think the abscess is moist due to the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces; then extract with fine pincers and a syringe, as we have said, so that the extraction may be lighter.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	 When water falls into the ear, it is necessary for the patient to sneeze first with condiments, and fill the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	 And let him lie on that same side where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	 if it jumps through this, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	 if this does not work, then take many small and light stones according to the length of your thumb, and heat them slightly over the fire; and have the patient place one of these stones into his ear canal, and jump on his feet from the other side, and strike another stone onto the stone that is in the ear; and do not stop doing this with the stones until all the water comes out, and thus it all comes out; and if you see, take a reed, and insert one end into the ear, and grab the other end with fire until the thinnest part of the reed is burnt; then repeat this process with other reeds until all the water comes out, as we have said in the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	 In the extraction of an insect, if it is small like a flea and similar things, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is large enough to be felt, then use the extraction of needles; and this is the easiest thing to remove that may be in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	 In the extraction of worms lodged in the ears, when you treat it as we have said in the division and in dealing with distillations, and the treatment does not help, then you must look at the ear towards the sun: if any worm appears, draw them out with fine needles, and if none appear, take the reed of which there is a form:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	 And let it be narrow below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	 And pour the most subtle liquid into the ear according to the quantity of the patient's suffering, then suck out all the pus; do this frequently until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	 And if they do not come out, then plug the pus with cotton as I have said in the previous section; and if they do not come out forcefully as we have said, then administer distillations that the ancients have proven for the killing of worms, and you will find them in the treatise on distillations; and then distill your oils and medicines into the ear with all this apparatus, whose shape is like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	 And let it be made of silver or copper with a small hole at the bottom, and on top a cover for distilling; and to press the distillation inside, use an instrument of copper well-made for this purpose. If you wish, take a scraper and wrap around its tip some cotton evenly; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever medicine you wish into the pus; and let the pus be in the ear; then insert the scraper all the way to the bottom of the cotton, and press your hand gently until the oil is distilled into the depths of the ear. And let the patient feel the warmth inside, and let the distillation be heated in a little pot over the fire before it is distilled into the ear; and take care that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be as good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	 Of ear blockage
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	 No child is born without any opening in the ears; and this same thing happens to men due to blockage from a wound or flesh growing inside the ear, and these blockages sometimes go deep into the ear so that you cannot see them; and sometimes there is a lack of the opening, and one can see it well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	 Therefore, those that go deep and cannot be seen are of serious harm in many situations. And those that can be seen should be treated by placing the patient's ear towards the sun; and look inside: if you see an apparent hair, then perform this entire procedure as described herein:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	 And let it be sharp and cutting both in front and behind entirely, so that it does not wound the ear; if the excision is of flesh or body of the ear, then hold it with fine pincers, and cut lightly, until all that flesh is completely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	 And if the excision is deep in the ear, then take a subtle and light razor and heat it slightly over the fire, then place it in the body of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	 If you feel the excision from which the patient feels pain at hearing, pierce lightly, and be careful not to harm the nerves of the ear; then place in the ear a tent according to the width of the opening, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Do this every day until the wound is healed, where you take a bandage and soak it in rose water, and sprinkle powdered vitriol on it; and if you see the ear swell up, then it is necessary that you remove the bandage and replace it with another bandage soaked in wax made from rose oil and beeswax, until the swelling disappears; then continue the treatment until it heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	 And if bleeding continues, soak a sponge in cold water and place it on the ear, and use other treatments that stop the bleeding which are in the treatise on distillations.
de la char des papieres	 of parchment
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	 This cataract that comes from the eyes when they are wet and then dry, it is necessary that you stretch them with tweezers and forceps, and scrape off a piece of its root with a spatula; then place powdered vitriol on the spot.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	 And if without skinning, then cauterize with the subtle lancet, and after the incision it is worth moving; and many times they return when something remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not come back.
de la gresle	 of the gravel
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	 Many times there come in the eyes things that seem like gravel in their form and hardness, and for this reason this disease is called "hail," and it is an accumulation of thick moisture in the eye above and below; the treatment is thus: take care if the hail moves from one side to another, and this is a minor thing to know; then make an incision wide enough, then lightly scarify each part, then take with forceps, and cut it off.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	 If you cannot cover it without piercing the skin a little, it does not harm the patient; and if the wound is large, join it with a stitch, and treat it until it heals; and if it is small, do nothing by force, for the ointment restores it quickly and generates flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	 If the grain descends into the ear towards the upper part, turn the skin, and spread the grain with tweezers, and cover and press it on both sides; and if the skin is separated by the incision, it does not matter; and when the grain is covered, wash the place with salt water, and treat it with that which generates flesh until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	 of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	 And exinach is a fat that accumulates on the sheets of paper above it, and this happens more in children than in any other person, and it greatly troubles their eyes, and in the mornings they come down with catarrh, and cannot look at the light of the sun because tears hasten to their eyes; and for this reason they lie down on their faces often, and sleep with their heads up, and their sheets beneath their pillow are moist from the exinach which appears in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	 And when you squeeze the place between your fingers and feel the exinach between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	 And the method of operation is that the patient places his head in your hand; and then take a cloth of linen, and prepare a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity that contains exinach from each part, then place it on him; and squeeze between your fingers on one side and the other, so that the exinach is gathered into the circle; then make in the middle of the moisture with a sharp spatula a slit as wide, and not larger than the wound made for bleeding a vein; and cut the skin through to the exinach; and in many cases exinach comes out of the slit, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	 Pull the cloth between your fingers, turning your hand to the right and left until it is spread out; and be careful not to enter the slit, so that you do not reach all the way to the eye, as you might injure it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	 And if the cloth does not open at the beginning of the slit, slightly widen the slit until it opens; then pull it as we have said, moisten clean rags in water, and place them on the spot, and bind with bandages.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	 And there are men who grind salt and put it on to corrupt that moisture which remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then continue the treatment until it is healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if it comes to the place of a hot abscess, then cure with soothing plasters until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	 of the hairs of the papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	 When in the eyes hairs arise other than natural ones, and they grow old, they harm the eyes and cause various diseases such as customary tears and softening of the eyelids and cataracts, to the point that it is the cause of the destruction of the eyes; and the cure is according to four methods: by cautery with fire, or by medicine as described in the chapter on cautery, and by incision and suturing or by canthus, as I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	 You must place the patient's head in your lap, then turn the eyelid of the eye towards your left hand; if it is turned over, that is good; but if not, then you put a needle through all one thread above; and let this be near the edge of the eyelid where the hairs grow near those hairs, and draw the thread across the entire eyelid, and turn it towards the razor; then make an incision in the lower part under the eyelid, under the misplaced hairs, cutting all the way to the large lacrimal gland down to the small one; then pull out the thread, and place a small tent of cotton and linen under the eyelid, then sign the upper eyelid with a figure, like the myrtle leaf, and nevertheless it is necessary that the figure be according to the amount you wish to raise the divided eyelid.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	 And if someone needs to cut off a large quantity of the skin according to how soft the skin is; then make an incision along all the spatula over the two lines that you have drawn, and begin from the big tear duct down to the small one; and let there be one of the cuts near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then insert the onion into one of the two angles of the heart, then scrape it all off; then bring together the two lips with a stitch of a very fine thread, and wipe away the blood, and make the excess threads adhere over the two eyebrows with some gluey things, if you wish to do this; and if not, then don't worry about it, but leave the stitch and the threads for three days or four; then treat the wound without a stitch with drying and constricting things, because the skin relives with the healing of the wound and its adhesion, but the stitch is harmful (as the ancients say), and this is work without fear; and there is another way: which is that you cut the skin in the shape of a myrtle leaf, as we have told, with three open onions according to the form which is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	 Then cut that which overhangs the small forces equally according to the form that is here.
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	 And if you cannot hold the tongs, and the thing is not equal, then take a needle with one thread, and insert it into the figure; and insert another thread next to the large lip, and the second thread next to the small one, and gather the threads equally between your fingers; then lift your hand equally, and lift all the skin on which you have marked, as we have said, then join the two lips of the wound by stitching, and continue the cure until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, then soothe it with cerate and similar ointments; and sometimes it happens that the hairs of the skin are turned: then you should use what we have said about the incision; but stitching in one way or another is more skillful.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	 Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: And the treatment of the chains is as follows: that you turn the paper and the opening inside according to what I have said, and then make two chains by art, and two subtle laces as long as the paper and wide as the spatula; and cut at the two ends where you hold the threads; then subtly join one with the other above what surmounts the paper of the eye, and strongly tighten the two chains from the two parts; and leave it thus for some days, and the skin that is tightened will die and blacken and rot, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	 If it delays, then cut with a forceps, and cure it until it is healed; and when the wound is closed, and the paper is removed, the hairs will no longer prick; and this is the form of the two chains that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity in length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	 The work is such that you should take a subtle needle, and put into it a soft and subtle silk thread; then assemble the heads and tie one and the other subtly, and let the length of the threads be one palm long; then arrange in the sheath another brief and subtle silk thread, and tie the head of the thread; then have the patient put his head on your hand; and let it be near the sun so that the work may be illuminated, for this is a subtle and small work. Then push the needle all along the sheath in the root of the hair close by, and make it pierce quickly in the skin until you draw it above the natural hair; then pull the hair up to above the sheath, and put into the sheath that hair, if there is one or two or three or more; then pull your hand so that the hairs come out all along the sheath in the skin with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	 And if the eyelash is treated and the hair does not grow with it, you will pull out the eyelash completely along with the entire thread that you had placed there, until the eyelash comes out strongly from above and you can see it through the eye's vision; then you will pull out the eyelash and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for 2 or 3 days, until the hair takes root in its place and the flesh grows over it; and if the hair is small, accompany it with one long natural hair from the eyebrows, and raise it with that one until it is elongated, then remove it.
de la porriture de l’oil	 of the eye's infection
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	 When this disease called "aleacrati" or eye infection occurs in the eye, there are two types: one is natural, and the other is unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	 And it happens suddenly from a wound, or from cutting, or from cautery, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	 And the manner of the work is that you split open that seam, and turn back its lips, and place inside linen tents, and bind it until it heals; and it is not necessary to use in his treatment things that dry out and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	 For if you do this, the disease returns worse than before; but use softening things, such as fenugreek; and let them be boiled in water or vinegar and flax seeds, and melted onions with any of the oils, and wrap it in a linen bandage, and heal it thus.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	 And the treasure of your cure is that you should beware lest it heal not according to the form that it was before; and these works that we have spoken of are nothing other than remedies for this illness, so that it does not return according to the form that it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	 of the flesh that comes in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	 This illness, which truly is called "axacrati", is both natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	 The accident comes from wounds and tears and cauterization and similar things; and the way to work on it is that you take a needle with two threads and insert it into the flesh, and have it pierce from the left tear duct to the right, so that the thread passes through two pieces of flesh; then apply the flesh above all the needle, and cut off a spatula-wide piece.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the shape of the skin returns as it should, that is good; if not, then take a razor and place it in the cut, and turn the skin, and make two cuts on each side inside the skin; and let the heads of the two cuts be at the two corners of the incision that you have made, and let them be arranged so that when they are assembled, the shape is like the shape of a letter that has the name "I griesche"; then remove that flesh, according to the quantity that its sides are sharp below, from which follows the skin, then join the two cut parts, and sew them with a wool thread; then follow the cure as we have said about softening medicines, and tents, until it is healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	 And if the disease comes from a split or stitch or cautery, then you must make a plain split beneath the hairs of the skin, according to what is written above; then heal between the two layers of a tent, as I have said; and the work should be done according to the form of the disease, for it varies greatly in form. The wise master prepares an instrument of all his power so that he may restore the figure to its natural shape; and the patient himself, according to what is necessary for the work and instruments in many dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	 from the joining of the skin
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When this joining occurs in such a way that the upper skin is joined with the white of the eye and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then you must insert the tip of a razor beneath the skin and lift it up; and hold it with pincers, until you cut what is above with a subtle spatula, which should not be too sharp nor too cutting, so that the patient may not suffer that the too sharp spatula hurt the eye; and your incision, by which you peel that assembly, should be light, so that the skin returns according to its natural shape; and all that assembly is healed, and sometimes in the eye it becomes salty, and lift with sweet water, and of collyrium; then put between the skin and the eye a linen tent, and place on the eye moist wool abundantly with egg; and after the third day use of collyrium and healing things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	 of the fingernail of the eye
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	 Know that the nail comes in two forms: one is nervous and similar to a hard syrup, and another which is not nervous but is like congealed white moisture; when touched with iron and tried to grasp with tweezers, no one can do it; and both forms begin towards the large tear duct, and grow little by little until they cover the entire eye, all the light, and the movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	 And the manner of the incision is that the patient puts their head in your lap, then they close their eyes. Lift the lid with your hand, then remove the nail with tweezers of small size, and hold it above; then take a needle, and put one horsehair, or cow hair, or ox hair in it, and a strong thread; and double the point of the needle a little and insert it into the nail, and pierce all the way through the nail with the needle, and tie the nail to a thread and hold it above, and scrape all the way up the side of the nail that follows the root and the silk of the hair to the head, then cut off the remaining part at the root of the tear duct all the way down to the subtle spatula and small forces, and leave the natural flesh in the tear duct, so that through the incision the body of tears does not usually come out; sometimes the nails are only held by the quick and by the thread, as we have said; then scrape with a soft spatula, the shape of which is this:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And beware that the spatula does not touch the fleshy tissue and tear it, and that the prunella is not pierced; and after the incision, throw into the eye a little bag of linen cloth, and made of lead, and leave it until the next day; then treat it as needed until it heals.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	 And if the nail is not soft enough and you cannot insert the needle, and the pincers cannot enter, this resemblance of a nail is often treated with medicine; and as I have said in the previous section, if you see it growing, then work on the patient's eye, and take a small, sharp spatula like this:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	 And scrape the nail gently from above, and if you see that it does not diminish and the reason approaches, then drip into the eye a collyrium made of lead oxide and red ochre ground together, and pack the eye until the next day; then resume the other work according to this same work, until it is all removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If nothing is wrong with the eye, such as an abscess, then leave it alone, and first cure the hot abscess until it is healed, then resume the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	 And if the appearance of the flesh of the eyelid appears in the eye to great harm, then suspend it with a hook, and cut off part of it but not all, so that no tears come into it; then drip into the eye red collyrium made from lead oxide.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	 Of the flesh that grows over the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	 Of the eye of some men grows sometimes red flesh, and covers the pupil and presses on the eyelids and turns them outward, and it seems like a rose of Balthazar; and the work is that the patient put his head in your hand, then you open the eyes, and pull all that flesh with suitable tweezers for this purpose, and hold it firm; then cut the first flesh, and continue cutting to the razor until the end, and be careful not to injure the eye during the operation; and let the incision of the spatula, as we have said in the incision of the nail and in small forces from which one removes a splinter, as this form shows after this chapter; and when the incision is completed and all the flesh is removed, fill the eye with oil of lilies or distill red-hot iron and similar corrosive medicines into it, and put on the eye thick cotton with egg white, so that it be secure against inflammation; and if anything remains and the pus overcomes you, and you doubt inflammation, leave the eye and treat the inflammation with soothing remedies; then return to your work until it is healed, and thus do when flesh grows in the eye in this manner.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	 But nonetheless it is necessary that you lift the treatment for each weak eye from the natural way; and in the work of iron, from the accidental way; and do not insert your hand into any of these works until you see that this limb can endure that work.
des voines des eulz	 of the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	 If they are red veins that cover the eye, and take away from sight its function and weaken the eye always.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	 Therefore, first consider whether the eye in which there is this vein is sound, and there is no other disease except for the vein; then treat the eye in this manner: instruct the patient to put his head in your lap, then raise those veins with a thread according to his knowledge, and let the thread be subtle double like this:  (Here the text would have a diagram or drawing showing how to place the thread.)
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	 And let there be two ounces by degrees in one body according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	 and when the veins have been strengthened in this way, bleed them hour after hour, until you see the strong veins move away from the eye; and be careful not to damage the eye with the points of the spatula; and do this work at noon before the sun, and be very diligent in your work so that you only cut those veins; and when you have done this, drip into the eye green and red choler to destroy what remains of the black.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	 And if you do not have the power to collect all of it in that hour, then make a plaster on the eye with soothing things for the pain of the eyes, and leave it for some days until the pain is soothed and there is a sure sign of hot abscess, then begin again in this manner which is before until it is healed; and this is the form of the forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	 Of the anal fistula
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	 The physicians call this «arissati» fistula: when you cure it by cautery and with burning medicine as I have said before, and it is not healed, then there is a need to incise over the abscess where it should die, and draw out all the moisture that is there, until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	 And when the bone is exposed, and you see the corruption and the blackness, then raise it with all the instrument that has this form; and it is called «sharp point», and it should be made of iron or steel, and it should be pointed like a file as it is in the present figure:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	 And place it on the site of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your fingers, and press your hand a little until you know that this corruption is raised; and do this several times, then restore the place with drying medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	 if the wound is healed, and flesh grows there, and the body of the blow remains thus for forty days, and it does not reopen nor become infected with any bad accident, know that it is healed; if not, then there is no other device than to bring the fistula back through the perineum in this manner: and it is that you uncover the bone a second time with iron, and with sharp medicines, and when it is uncovered, then take a graft in this manner, and let the head of the iron be at three angles, and let the stem be thinned to the top as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	 then place it on the bone near the margin, and keep your hand one pace from the eye, then turn all the graft until it pierces the bone, and the patient feels this because the wind comes out if he holds his hand over his nose; and then restore the place with dry medicines, as I have taught you, and when the flesh grows and hardens the place, the matter goes to the nose; thus, it is a lighter burden on the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	 of the exit of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When the eye is completely open and there is no disturbance or diminishment, you must bind the patient; then heal it, then apply cupping glasses without pricking to draw out [fluids], then place on the eye a plaster made of alum, aloe, incense, and mastic, and then press the eye, and bandage with compresses and cloths; and the method of the cloths is such that you take enough cloths, and double each one four times, and then put one on top of the other according to the quantity that the eye needs; then press with a very hard bandage, and reapply the cupping glasses without pricking; then remove the cupping glasses and leave the eye pressed day and night, and if the plaster softens, you must press it very much; then remove the plaster after the day and night, and if you see the eye healing, that is good; if not, then resume the plaster and the cloths and the plaster and the cupping glasses until it heals.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	 Of the breaking of woven cloth
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 When disruption comes in the woven cloth, it opens and exudes resinous matter like grains of sand, which is dreadful to behold; then if you see it covered, the work is such that you drive a needle through the root of the part below until it reaches the upper part, then insert another needle where there is a double thread from the edge of the cloth; and make it perforate, and leave the first needle according to its position; then cut around the double thread and tie one end of the woven cloth around it, and tighten it well, then remove the needle and place a moistened linen cloth soaked in egg on top; and let it be until the threads adhere to the cloth, then treat the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is restricted by the woven cloth around each part of a circle of cloth until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the eye gives a great appearance of it, pierce it with a subtle spatula that reaches to the depth of the eye, and let out the turbid moisture, and let it descend the eye, and enter in quickly; then draw out until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	 from the bottom of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	 This disease which is called "alcunnati" is nothing but the humour gathered in the eye, resembling descending water, and it is not water; and the manner of the appearance of this work is such that you make the patient sit on a well-prepared and upright seat, then take the head between your hands from two sides, and move it so that you see the humour coming above your eyes; then let it be inserted, and do not let it descend, and let the light be uncovered, and may the patient see things as he used to; and if it does not descend below, know that it is water, and if the descent of the humour is not prepared as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 if you seat the patient between your hands, then take a thin spatula and make an incision on the horny tissue at the junction of the conjunctiva with the horny tissue and the cornea, until the abscess comes out; and when it is out, instill hot water mixed with honey into the eye, or water boiled with fenugreek and honey, then cure it with another cure until it heals.
des aigues de l’oil	 of the waters of the eye
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	 We have seen similar cases in the section on division, and these are those that need to be pierced; do it according to the health of the patient.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	 It is necessary that you make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from the light of the sun; and bind the healthy eye tightly; then place the eyelid of the affected eye in your left hand if it is the left eye, or in your right hand if it is the right eye; then take in your right hand, if it is the left eye, the instrument called "almagda", or in your left hand if it is the right eye; then place the tip of the instrument near the cornea by the thickness of a ray at that white part of the eye towards the inner corner, then thrust the instrument called "almagda" vigorously, and turn your hand until it pierces the white of the eye, and feel that almagda reaches the empty place; and it is necessary that the measure of the almagda's path be to the depth of the measure of the space which is from the eyelid to the end of the black; and this is the cornea of the eye; you will see the bone in that eyelid through the clarity of the horny tissue, and then place the instrument until it reaches the spot where the water is, then press it under a path after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	 if water flows now, then the patient sees before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	 After a short rest, and if the water rises again in the second way, place the finger with the instrument, and when it is inserted and does not rise, gently extract the almond by turning your hand little by little; then put a little salt in the water, and raise the eye out of this.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	 Then place over the eye a compress or wet wool in rose oil and plenty of egg, and bind with healthy oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	 We, and those of our time, use horseradish with plenty of egg.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	 And if the almond cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, for there are such men who have very hard eyes, then you must take the instrument called "alberit," which has this shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	 And so pierce the conjunctiva only, and do not go too deep into it, but make the place subtle, then put almagda in it, as we have said; and at the end of the work prepare for the patient a suitable sleeper, in which he sleeps on his back in a dark place; and let him be deprived of all movements, and let him take light foods, and do not move his head to the right or to the left, and let him be tied according to his disposition until the third day; then untie him in that same dark house, and test his sight, and show him some things, and then put the bandage back on until the seventh day; and it is not necessary that you do this at the hour of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you lighten it, because the water rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	 If abscesses come, dislodge the eye before the seventh day, and apply the remedy that soothes abscesses; and when it is soothed, uncover the eye and place a small ring on its edge to cover for some days, and always keep it in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	 And then come out of the house little by little, and return to its usual state; and know that no disciple should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	 And one came to us who was from Yrach, who told us that in his country they made almagda, for which they drew water; but nevertheless I have never seen any in our land, nor read of it in the books of the ancients; and perhaps this is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	 Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, pour ceux qui ne les connaissent pas, afin qu'ils puissent les voir; et soient en cuivre pur.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	 And the heads of them should be of this same subtlety, and the rears in three acute angles.
de la char sor le neis	 on the flesh above the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	 Sometimes hairs grow on the nose in different places, which makes some look like scorpions with many legs; and there are such that have flesh of red color, and some soft flesh of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	 Then for that soft hair which is not hard, it is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; and open his nostrils, and pour the ointment on those hairs, and pull them out; then cut with what you can support in a subtle sharp spatula on one side, until you know that all that flesh is removed.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	 And if any substance remains that cannot be healed, then open it with all the fine instruments lightly, so that nothing remains; and if it swells or has an abscess, then let the pus out as needed; and if it is malignant abscesses, then hurry and cauterize until the blood is darkened and all the flesh is removed, then pour cold water and vinegar or wine over it.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	 If pus comes out and moisture reaches the palate, know that it is healed; and if the moisture does not come out as needed, know that there is new flesh on the bone above, which the instruments cannot cut: then it is necessary to put a thick thread of linen in, and let it be knotted by hand, and each knot should have a finger's width or less space; and let the patient put the end of the thread into his nostril with all his might, and pull while smelling until it comes out through the nostril into the mouth; and many times children do this in school, and it is an easy thing for one who wants to do it; then hold the end that comes out of the nostril in one hand, and the other end that comes out of the mouth in the other hand, and know one after the other by feeling them like us who are on the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	 Do this so that you know that the knots have corrupted that flesh; then draw out the thread, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread with Egyptian unguent, and put it back in the nose as before; do this for 3 days or more, until the unguent has corroded all that remains of the flesh; and then put a lead plug in the nose for some days until it is healed, and if there is need for drying medicines, use them; and this is the shape of the instrument to clean out the head, into which one distills oils and medicines into the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	 And whether it is of silver or brass, resembling an open lamp, like a plug, and the conduit likewise; and if you wish, make a closed plug, and let the instrument be full to clean out the head; and have one handle on top to hold it when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	 of the flesh on the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	 often occurs on the tip of the nose a disease called "telul", and it grows and becomes large very quickly, so that it is a visible thing to behold; therefore it is necessary to cut it at the beginning, and remove all the pus, then apply cautery or burning medicine on the spot; and if one delays cutting until it is large, it is wise to check if it is hard, of fiery color, of poor quality: do not touch it with iron because it is a burnt abscess, for when one cuts it sometimes, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is of soft texture, not of fiery color, and you see that it can be completely cut out, let the patient empty himself and cut without fear, and treat the place with drying and astringent substances.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	 when the nose is cut and bruised
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	 Know that when a solution for continuity comes to one of these cartilaginous works, it profits little, except in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Therefore, when this happens to someone, first consider if the wound is fresh and bleeding; then join the two lips with a stitch, and cure it until it heals; and if the lips are already separated from one part to another, then you must burn all the parts of their skin until they heal, then join the two lips with a stitch, and hold them firmly, and sprinkle on powdered dragon's blood and crushed incense; and place a piece of strong plaster or other adhesive plaster on the powders, and let it sit until it falls off by itself, then cure it with ointment until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.
