It is therefore necessary to avoid the cure of iron, and that which is at the top should also be avoided; and in one who has a swelling of the artery, make an incision on the skin above it; then work the tail under the nails, and neatly separate the artery from the membranes until it is exposed; then insert below it a needle and have it pierce to the other side and constrain the artery with a double thread in two places, according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples; then puncture the place between the two ties with an intromitter until the pus comes out, and let the abscess be relieved; then administer the cure as if it were a boil, until the ties fall off; then treat it like any other wound, until it is healed. And if the abscess is due to the incision of the vein, it is necessary that you dye in your hand whatever you can of the abscess on all the skin, then insert the needle under the place you are holding in your hand, and have it pierce, and there should be a double thread so that you draw it from the other side; then bind the abscess as I have told you with the tie of one part of the two threads to the other side of the filament; and if you doubt that the thread will not come out, then insert another needle along all of one thread under the entire abscess at the incision of the first needle, and constrain the threads in four places; then cut the abscess until the superfluous comes out, then cut the superfluous skin and leave what is tied; then place a cloth moistened in wine and oil on top, then administer cures of bandages and dressings until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	 of nerve abscesses
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	 Similarly, as an abscess can occur in the artery and vein, so too can an abscess form in the nerves when they are wounded or subjected to excessive strain, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	 And this happens more often in the shoulders and feet, and in all places where there are joints, and it is a serious abscess, and its color resembles the color of flesh, and it has many dispositions without pain; and when one presses it firmly, the patient feels pain, and it is not deep within the body, but below the heart; and it moves well from all sides, and does not go forward or backward, or down or up, and that which is in joints should not be struck with iron: perhaps a contraction would occur; and that which is in the head or forehead, pierce the skin with a lancet.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the abscess is small, hold it with tongs and cut into its root; and if it is large, suspend it on an onion, peel it, then remove it and close the wound with stitches, and care for it until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	 of hanging boils
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	 Sometimes it happens in the belly and not elsewhere, and this is a disease called "fungus" because of its similarity to them, and its root is delicate, and its head is large; and there are small ones and very large ones; and I saw a man who had two in his belly which were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had a thin root, and they were always split open, and moisture flowed out of them constantly.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	 I cut them and found one weighing eighteen ounces, and the other six ounces. The work in the incision is such that you observe if the patient is moist, and the color of the artery is white and moist and of a subtle root; then cut it with a broad spatula, and in your presence let there be the cauterizer on fire.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	 For in cutting, there often comes too great a flow of blood, and if the wound overpowers you, then hasten to cauterize; and if you see the patient frightened and fearful of the iron incision, then take a well-made linden thread and tie the artery as we have said, and leave it for two days; and then tighten it, and do not cease to tighten the linden thread until it cuts the artery, and each through itself without labor; and if the roots are thick, there is fear in cutting, but you can cut half of it, then cauterize so that it does not return; then treat the wound, and beware that you do not cut the vein which is of a reddish color and of weak sense and milky appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	 Car this is an encrusted boil, and I will come to the cure of boils later.
quant li boude ist fuer	 When the pustule is strong
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	 If the appearance of the pustule comes from a burn of a wound or from a tear in the skin due to syphilis, and it is on the abdomen and some of the boils, as happens in other ruptures, whether of blood flowing from veins or arteries according to what was said before, or from flatulence; and if it is from the rupture of the skin and the issue of the pustule, then the color of the boil resembles the color of the body, and it is a slight thing without pain, and opens in various ways.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	 And if it is from the issue of the intestine, then it is more varied, and when one presses it with their fingers, it resists, and then returns, and perhaps swells, and greatly increases at the entrance to the bath and due to intense labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	 And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing, and it is evident when you press it in your hand, do not force it; and if it is due to blood, then the abscess appears by these signs: large and hard, and it is fixed according to a certain amount; and if it is due to flatulence, then it is soft to the touch, and the work is such that you look at whether the appearance is of the blood of the artery, or of the vein, or of flatulence.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	 Then you must leave the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	 For there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter on abscesses, concerning the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	 And if the appearance is of the intestine or the bladder, then you must instruct the patient to hold his hand, and be stretched out straight; then sign around the opening entirely; then command him to lie down gently between your hands, then go all around the place you have marked with the entire spatula, then press half of the abscess above the large hook; then tie it around with a strong thread or a strong silk cord firmly, and let the knot of the tie be loose; then work half of the abscess stretched out over the tie, and put your index finger in, and search for the intestine; if you find it caught by the tie, then untie it, and push the intestine outside the stomach; and if you find the bladder, then take it with the hook, and cut off the excess; and if the artery or the vein makes it difficult, go around well, then return to your work and take two needles, and put in two strong threads, and put the two needles around what you have done in a cross that you make perforate; then press the abscess in four places over the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the place until it becomes rotten, and let the dead flesh fall off by itself; or you cut when it has become subtle and rotten, then cure the abscess as we have said; and draw out the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the place as it should be cured, and close the place. 》
dou chancre	 Of the cancer
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	 We have said in the division of similarities to cancer, and how one should work with medicines therein, and how one must avoid the iron cure; and we say that cancer invades the flesh, and great care is needed in its treatment, and the ancients said that when a cancer is in a place where it can be scraped off, like a cancer on the breasts, and in the thighs, and similar places, and one should remove all of it when it is in its beginning; and when it is large and old, then you must not approach it, for I have never seen anyone healed from it; nor has anyone been healed from it before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And the treatment, when it is in a place where it can be removed, as we have said, is that you first purge the patient of black bile; then make him fast if he has an obvious fullness, then prepare the patient well for the treatment; then cast your onions on the cancer, and shave all around it, and remove it from all sides without leaving anything behind; and let the blood flow freely, and press the place well with your hand or with something else, and if the bleeding is contrary to the cutting of the artery or vein, then cauterize until the blood is stopped; then treat him with other treatments until he is cured.
de ydropisie	 of the dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	 We have already said in the division the similarities of dropsy, and in what manner the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each similarity, and the cure that is done by medicine, and that which is done by iron: only eclites is mentioned; and one should not touch with iron in these two similarities: namely, tympanites and ascites, because it is a deadly thing; therefore when you treat this similarity of dropsy called "eclites" with medicines, and the cure does not benefit, then look to see if the patient is weak, or if he has another illness besides dropsy, such as fever and similar things; then do not touch with iron, because there is doubt; and if you see that the patient is of great strength, and he has no other illness than dropsy alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you should act thus: lift the patient upright in your hands, and have the assistant press the belly outwards towards the lower part of the foot, then take the pointed spatula in this manner:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	 And let it be cut from two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	 and at the point, yet not so deeply that it may reach the intestines when inserted, nor injure them; then observe whether the dropsy is directed towards the intestines: if so, your incision should be above the navel three fingers' breadth to the right of the navel; and if the dropsy is due to liver disease, let your incision be on the left side of the navel three fingers' breadth; and if it is due to spleen, let it be on the right, and it is not necessary that the patient lie upon the incision so that the superfluous humors may run to the weak place; then perforate all the skin with the instrument, and push it through, and lift your hand to the whole membrane between the skin and the flesh as if scraping off a quantity of one nail or around it; then pierce the flesh until the membrane reaches the proper place, which is the place of water, then draw out strongly, and into this instrument whose form is here:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	 And it is similar to a fine silver wire, and it is of light bronze or brass; and in the lower part there is a small hole; and on one side three holes; and two on the other side, and one on another side; and the head is cut like a quill, and this is the shape of the incision that the scribe cuts the quill with:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	 at the top is the ampule, so that when the instrument comes to the water, it then goes up on the instrument; empty now half or a third, for if you empty more than is needed in that hour, by chance the patient may die from the resolution of his spirit with the weapon, or he falls into a faint, or he approaches death; but empty according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the patient signify, and his pulse; then remove the instrument and retain the water, and it is retained now by the cork which stops the hole that is on the syphon, as I have said, that you pierce in this manner; then begin again with the instrument the next day, if you see the patient suffering thus, and draw a little water; do this every day, and beware of wasting so much that it does not remain but for a bit of water.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	 And if you doubt the patient, and you leave a lot of water, cure him with the burial in hot sand, and by sweating profusely or bathing in the sun, and dye it with wine; and cure with desiccative medicines until he is healthy, and cauterize on the stomach and liver and spleen after removing the water, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	 Of the obstruction of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	 Sometimes children are born without an opening in the penis, or the opening is small, or it is not in its proper place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	 If he needs to be pierced immediately with a very fine needle according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	 then put into the opening a subtle cloth of linen, and tie it and hold it thus for three days or four; and when he wants to make urine, let the cloth be removed, and make urine, and then put it back; and perhaps it is not necessary, for the urine that comes forth does not leave it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	 He whose opening is small, let him be treated with the linen cloth, as we have said, and it will widen.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	 Those who do not have the opening in its proper place are afflicted, for some are born with the opening at the tip of the penis, which prevents them from urinating forward unless they lift their penis up; and they cannot ejaculate because the matter cannot reach the vagina, and this is a serious illness.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And the way of working is that the patient lies on his back, then the head of the rod and the cup are extended as much as the width of a feather, so that the hole meets in the middle, as it should; and beware of bleeding that often occurs there, and if it happens, staunch it with what staunches blood, and treat the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	 of the pustules on the rod
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Often these abscesses come in the rod, and it is an ugly appearance of flesh; there are malignant and non-malignant ones; thus you must take them at one time with subtle oil, and cut and clean all, then apply cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment; then treat with refined ointment until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	 And if the bath is foul, of bad color and stinking, then it is necessary that you bring a cautery to it.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	 When you have cut it, and if the bath is partly within the blade and partly outside of it, then it is necessary that you first remove the bath which is inside; and when it is healed, then treat what is outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 For when you treat it together, it is not certain that the head of the blade will not be pierced, and blackness and corruption will come to the blade and the wound; therefore, cut away all that is black and corrupt, then apply a plaster of honey and flour made from pomegranate bark and vetch, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	 And if blood follows from bleeding, then apply the lunar cautery according to this manner.
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	 The cautery helps in two conditions together: that is to say, for bleeding and for corruption; and if the glans of the penis is corrupted and retracted, it is necessary that you insert a leaden tube into the urethra of the penis, and the patient urinates through it. And when the hair on the head of the penis (which happens to those who have not been circumcised), occurs due to a wound or an abscess, then it is necessary that you peel it with one instrument, until the foreskin is freed, and the glans of the penis is liberated from all sides. And if it is difficult to do this, then peel with a spoon some of the head of the penis and the skin; then dry gently between two things, and put a fine cloth of linen moistened in cold water, so that it does not adhere again.
de la circoncision	 of the circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	 Circumcision is not a separation of continuity like other wounds; however, when we perform this work willingly, and especially in children, it is necessary that we do the best and lightest work for healing.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	 I say that the ancients did not speak of the circumcision of their children, for they do not practice it in their law, and we only know what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	 For I have seen the majority of masters and barbers who perform circumcisions around Dal, and the foreskin, and the whole prepuce; thus blood flows because there are two layers, and by chance one cuts the upper layer and the lower one remains.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	 Or in this case, cover it, and the pain is doubled, and at the mundification which is from the nail, the point of the member is not secure; and at the mundification of the fingernail perhaps the iron will slip, and the work will go astray, and many times they are born in such a way that there is no need for mundification, and I have seen it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	 From the mundification which is done with files, I have found the benefit of the experiment, because the files cut as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 For when you press your hand and cut evenly in all directions throughout the whole time; but let the wire be well tightened around the skin; and let the manner of the first work be such that you make the child, if he understands, think that you are only tying the wire around the rod, and then release it in all the ways that you can; then hold it straight between your hands, and reassemble the files between your hands or under your feet so that the child does not see them or any of the instruments; then put your hand on the rod and blow into the heart, and pull it up until the head of the rod is in; then clean it well of the dirt that has accumulated there, then bind the place tightly with a double thread, then tie it under one finger to another ligature; and hold it between the two ties for the second ligation at the thumb and the little finger, and cover between the two ties, then lift the heart quickly and pull out the head of the rod; then let the blood run little by little, for this is the mother; and put powder on it and on the powder a piece of cloth glued with a yolk of boiled egg tempered with rose water, confected with good fresh oil, and leave it until the next day, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	 The shape of the strength for this purification is as follows: the two heads should be sharp and cutting, and the heads should be as large as the hand equally.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	 The error in the purification is when the heart goes to the incision; then it is necessary that you extend it with your fingernail before the place forms an abscess; and cut it equally, and if you cannot hold it with your fingernail, then hold it with tweezers, and then cut.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	 And if they exceed three days, and that which is below the penis is swollen, then leave it until the abscess is calmed, and lightly peel off the skin; then cut as much as you can move, and be careful of the penis part, for this will not harm him.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Cure then the place of sudden wounds with powder, as we have said in the treatment of powders, and if you cut the heart excessively and it goes above, it will not harm; cure it then, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	 regarding the retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	 The retention of urine is due to the obstruction of stones, or congealed blood, or bone, or dead flesh, or similar things, as we have said in the division; and if the urine is not released, and you see that the retention is due to a stone stuck in the neck of the bladder, then it is necessary that the patient be bent over his knees; and let his feet be placed on his back, and extend his belly from the part above the back, and let the patient strain as much as he can; and then the neck of the bladder is constrained to expel the stone upward, by which the urine is released; and if it does not come out, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must apply extraction with all the instrument called "syringe," of which here is the form: and let it be made of fine silver, lightly ribbed like the feather of a bird; and let the tube be one and a half palms long, and let it be fine at the end.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	 And the manner of the exit of the urine is such that you take a double thread, and tie it to the head of a wool or cotton bag, and insert the head of the thread into the syringe; and cut off the excess wool and push it up to the head of the syringe, then anoint the syringe with oil or butter and egg yolk, and make the patient sit on a seat, and wet his bladder and penis with moist oil and olive oil and tepid water; then gently insert the syringe into the penis until it reaches the root of the penis, then double the penis back towards the scrotum; then push the syringe forward into the bladder, and the patient feels it coming to the empty space, and this is not done except according to this order for fear that the path by which it goes is crooked; then draw out all the wool little by little, and the urine follows the wool, then remove it, and let the urine flow; and repeat with the syringe until the bladder is emptied, and the patient is relieved.
des maladies de la vessie	 Of the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	 When there are scorching or blood in the bladder, or rotting is gathered there, and you put water and medicine to distill, do it all with an instrument called a “clepsydra”, which looks like this:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	 It is sealed and has III openings: II on one side, and I on the other, as you can see. And let the place through which the medicine passes be such that it stops the rod well without addition, so that one can draw out the moisture and insert when necessary; and when you want to put your medicines in the bladder, place the head of the kestor in the moisture, and pull on the pulling that is inside. Thus, you will draw the moisture into the kestor, then push the pulling back in strongly; thus, the moisture will enter, and it will come to the bladder now, so that the patient feels it. And this is the shape of the subtle enema by which one enemates the bladder: it is like this:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	 And it is of silver or gold, and the head is higher; and beneath to the breast where the tie falls; then take a sheep's bladder and put the moisture in which you want to enema the bladder, then bind it between the two breasts firmly with a double thread, and warm the bag of this moisture on the fire; then insert the head of the enema into the penis, then press your hand on the bladder until all the moisture comes out evenly, as long as the patient feels that the moisture has come to the bladder; and if you do not have the bladder, then take a piece of parchment, and make it into a circle, and pierce it cleanly around; then insert a strong thread through these holes, then assemble the circle like an ale pot, and put inside what you want of oil and moisture and water, and bind it in the instrument; and do as you have done with the bladder, to press with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	 of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	 We have already spoken in the division about the types of stones and their extraction along with medicines; and I have explained the difference between bladder stones and kidney stones, and all the signs, and on which stone one should work with a scalpel; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	 I say that the stone which is formed in the bladder happens more often in children, and it is a sign when the urine comes out of the bladder like subtle water; and there is sand, and the patient's penis is heavy, and he has to urinate frequently, and then he retains; and at many of these discharges the foundation is laid; and the cure is light in children until they are four years old, and it is very serious in the elderly, and it is moderate in those who are between youth and old age; and the treatment is lighter for those who have a large stone than for those who have a small one.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	 And when we come to the treatment, it is first necessary to cleanse the patient with an enema, in order to draw out all the impurities that are in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	 Because sometimes it hinders in seeking the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	 Then take the patient by the feet and lift them up, moving them downwards, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and sometimes exits from above; then let him sit between your hands prepared, and his hands should be under his thighs, so that the bladder is tilted downwards; then search for it and touch inside; if you feel the stone in the area, hasten now to cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	 And if it does not fall with the touch, then moisten your finger of the left hand with oil, if the patient is a child, or your middle finger, if the patient is an adult; and put it in his anus, and seek the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, bring it to the neck of the bladder; then press on your finger, and push it out where you wish to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	 And instruct the attendant to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to stretch the testicles upwards with his right hand, and with his left hand remove the skin under the testicles in the area where the cut is made; then push the spatula into place, for this is the form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	 And it occurs between the testicles and the anus, not in the middle but on the left side of the vein; and let it be straight on the stone, and your two fingers should always be on the anus, and let the cut be across so that it is wide from outside, and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, not too large; perhaps this pressing with the finger that is on the anus makes it come out without effort; and know that there are such stones with angles and edges: they are difficult to remove; and there are those that are below, similar to a bean, and round, whose exit is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	 To that which has angles and edges, make the cut larger; and if it does not come out, then you must use pincers with sharp tips like a file to squeeze the stone so that it does not escape; or you push a subtle instrument curved at the tip underneath; and if you cannot trick it this way, then enlarge the pocket at the opening, and if the flesh peels off, then tighten it with vitriol; and if there are more than one stone, then first push the largest one towards the neck of the bladder, then cut above it, then pull it out forcefully, and the smaller ones afterwards if there are several.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	 And if it is very large, then it must be sewn shut, and make a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	 For two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or urine flows continuously in such a way that the wound cannot heal; however, you must try to pull it out, or cut it into pieces with pliers, until you pull it out in pieces; and when you have completed your work, fill the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and hold it shut, and put on top a cloth soaked in oil and wine, or oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the hot abscess; then lay the patient back on his pillow, and do not untie the bandage until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when you dislocate it, wash very well the place with oil and water, then treat it with ointment of lavender and ointment of basil until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	 And if there are abscesses or ulcers in the wound and blood clots in the bladder, and if urine is retained to the point that it leaves without jumping: insert your finger into the wound and remove that blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder. Then wash the wound with water and vinegar and honey, and help him in all the ways you know, until he is healed; and it is necessary that every time you treat him, you bind the two thighs together and apply the medicines to the place.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	 And if the stone is small, and it is in the passage of the bladder, and implanted therein, and urine cannot come out; then cure it as I say earlier, that you cut many times, for this cure excuses from cutting.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	 I have already proven so.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	 Take an iron rod according to this shape, and it should be fitted with three pointed tips at one end:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	 then take a thread and tie it around the rod below the stone, so that it cannot go back into the bladder; then gently push the rod into the bladder until it reaches the stone; and turn the rod in your hand little by little against the stone, until you can pierce the stone from the other side; then the urine will come out, and press your hand on what remains of the stone that is inside the bladder.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If it breaks immediately and is expelled with the urine, the patient is healed; and if you cannot do this for any reason that hinders it, then tie a thread under the stone and another on top, then make a rod towards the stone between the two threads, then pull out the stone, and remove the thread, and clean the congealed blood that is in the wound; and treat it until it heals.
de la piere des femmes	 of the woman's stone
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	 It rarely happens that a stone is found in women, and when it does happen, the treatment is difficult and hindered by three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a skilled woman who undresses before the doctors, especially when she is modest.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	 And the third manner is such that by chance one cannot find a woman skilled in this art of hands; and the fourth manner is such that the stones of the woman are more deeply located than those of the man, which is why a deeper incision must be made, and there is great fear involved. And if necessity requires it, you must seek a midwife well-versed in this, and one is hard to find, and if you cannot find one, then seek a subtle male physician; and present him with a wise old woman who has knowledge of women's life, or a woman who knows part of the art, and instruct her to do what you command regarding the investigation of the stone; and carefully consider if the woman is a virgin: then she must insert her finger into the vagina and search for the stone; and if she finds it, she must constrict it under her finger, and advise her to insert her finger into the vulva of the patient, and search and press her left hand strongly upon the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	 If she finds it, she must move it from kidney to kidney from the entrance of the bladder downwards, until it reaches the root of the thigh; then cut above the stone at the root of the thigh towards the middle of the con, where it is most fitted, and feel the stone in that part; and do not move her finger above or below the stone, and let the incision be small at first; then push the reed into the incision, if you feel the stone, press the wound strongly until the stone can come out forcefully, and know that there are many types of stones: namely, small and large, sharp and smooth, long and round, and with corners.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	 If you know the signs, you will know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	 And if the blood flows strongly, then place vitriol powder on the spot and hold it there for an hour until the bleeding stops; then return to your task until the stone is broken, and have the tools I told you about in removing stones from men to help you with your work; and if the blood flows strongly, and it is from a cut artery, then place powder on the spot and bind with cloths and bandages, and do not attempt this again, and leave the stone and do not remove it, for the patient may die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	 And when the heat of the blood is calmed and the place is dry, return to your work until the stone is broken.
de hernie carnouse	 Of a fleshy hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	 Aquous ramice is nothing other than a collection of moisture or white syphac, which is under the skin of the scrotum, containing the testicle; and it is called "syphac", and sometimes it is properly in the membrane of the testicle, so that one thinks it is another testicle; and this is the skin of the testicle between the white syphac that we have said; and these do not usually occur without a pouch.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	 And the generation of this ramice is due to weakness in the testicles, causing that substance to spread.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	 And sometimes it occurs due to a blow to the testicles, and this moisture has many colors: yellowish, without red, black, or whitish, and this happens more often; these are the signs to recognize this collection, for if it is in the white syphac that we have said, then the abscess is reasonable, a long pouch similar to the shape of a testicle, and the scrotum does not open, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	 And if there is moisture in the proper skin, then the abscess swells with part of the egg, and for this reason it is thought to be another egg; and if the moisture is between the leather of the thighs and the white flesh, one feels it well. Therefore, when you want to know the color of the moisture, try the entire intromission square, from which the form comes before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	 According to what follows after the intromission, judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when we cure it with iron, it is necessary that the patient be bled according to his ability and the fullness of his body; then place him on his back, on something a little high, and put many cloths under him; then sit on his left side, and command the assistant to sit on the right, and extend the rod along one of the two ribs at the base of the thighs; then take the spatula knife, and cut the leather of the thighs lengthwise from top to bottom until near the knee, and let your incision be entirely straight by dividing the leather of the thighs up to the white flesh, and delicately remove it as much as you can; then pierce the white flesh full of water with a wide hole, and draw out all the water, and then place your thumbs, and extend the white flesh upward; and do not touch the base of the thighs, but only the white flesh. Cut all or in pieces the same way delicately along his side, so that if you do not cut it cleverly, the water will come back; and if the egg jumps out of your work, place it back in its place when you have completed the work on the white flesh; then sew together the two lips of the base of the thighs with one stitch, then cure him as the other wounds, until he is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	 And if you find the egg corrupted by another illness, then it is necessary that you tie the vessels that are suspended, in fear of blood loss; then cut the ion to all the suspended parts, and extract the egg, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	 And if the vein is divided into two parts together, know that these are two branches; then cut the other part equally as you did the first, then wipe away the blood, and put on the wound linen moistened in rose oil; and put outside another linen moistened in wine and oil, and put on the two ions, and put on top doubled cloths, and bind it all with a bandage according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	 Then take two bandages, and fill them with wool scraps according to this likeness and let them be sewn together at the waist of the breeches; and one of the ends should go under the buttocks up to the back, and the other at the wrist; and the other two heads on the two sides, and all the fastenings should be gathered in the loop of the breeches. And sometimes this bandage is used for cautery instead of iron cutting; and it is that you take a subtle cautery knife, and cut the skin of the scrotum, and let it be heated as we have said, so that the white silk that contains the water is uncovered; then take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that silk at the ankles, and peel with this hot subtle cautery.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	 And cut in all ways that you can, until you have cauterized everything; and ensure that the fire does not touch the testicle; and know that this work is safer; and beware of the drawbacks of blood flow, and scars caused by the surgery; and if anything goes wrong, such as an abscess or blood flow or something else, then cure what is going wrong, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	 And if the patient is fearful and does not want to undergo this treatment due to its dreadfulness, then introduce a perforation, as I tell you. And it is that when you are certain through the indications we have mentioned that serous water is present there, make the patient sit on a high seat; then pierce the abscess in the lower part with the entire width of the sounding instrument, and insert the perforation into the body cavity; and let the opening be large so that all the liquid flows out. Then place cotton on the spot, bind it, and leave it to drain the remaining liquid; then treat it until the wound is healed; and if the white cloth does not allow the liquid to exit at the mouth of the wound, then you must insert a quill or the instrument used to draw water from hydrocephalic patients, the form of which has been described before. And widen the opening of the wound, and know that the liquid returns and is collected again after six months or thereabouts, and when it is collected as before, then the patient will pass the rest of his days.
de l’aposteme des coions	 of the abscess of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	 Know that in the incision of this vein, there is fear in many positions, so it seems to me that it is better left alone; and I will tell you about the work and likenesses of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	 I say then that many abscesses come in the body, and especially in the testicles; and this happens in many cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	 That is to say, it comes from an acute and bitter surplus that is spread to the testicles, or from a blow; and the color of the abscess varies according to the color of the body; and there is no pain, but the abscess is serious; and sometimes the abscesses are serious, frightening, and full of pus, and of dark red color, and sometimes it comes from a knot in an artery, or from an inflammation of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	 When it is by the narrowing of an artery, it is known by the hot swelling of an abscess when you press it against your fingers; and it is not necessary that you touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	 Those who are made of venous swelling are known by their disposition at the touch of the fingers, and one can well make the cut on this likeness, and on other limbs; and it is that you cut the heart of the kidneys, then push the egg upwards, and draw out the white with force, and deliver the suspensory from all parts of the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	 If the egg is already hardened with these limbs born, it is then necessary that you draw out the egg and cut it; and if it is in the air or in those which are inside the vessels, it is necessary that you deliver all that vein, and cut it roundly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	 And if the base of the flesh is in the rear place, then you must cut it all, and extract the egg, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when your work is completed, fill the wound with wool soaked in rose oil and wine, then cure it with other remedies until he is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	 of the abscess of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	 This is an abscess wrapped in a sheath resembling a bud, along with the softening of the testicles, and the patient becomes very ill when he walks; and the cure for this disease is almost as dangerous as the one mentioned before, but nevertheless we will tell you its treatment according to what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	 It is necessary that you make the patient sit on an elevated seat, then place the suspension of the testicles down to your thighs, including all the vessels near the penis, and hold them tightly and stretch them greatly; then cut with a sharp spatula along the length of the vessels until they are exposed, and then peel from each side, as we have said in the extraction of arteries located in the temples; then insert a needle where there is a double thread, and tie it at the first place where the vein has come out, and tie again at the other end; then cut straight in the middle according to the length of the body, and draw out the corrupt humors; then treat the wound as with others where one vein flows, so that none of the vessels flow where they nourish one of the testicles; for by this no harm comes, and if in all the vessels comes blood, it is necessary to pull out the testicles at all the vessels; so that the bird does not lose its nourishment due to the incision of the vessels, and dry up and cannot help.
de la routure dou syfac	 of the rupture of the shoulder
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	 The happenings of this rupture are through the section that comes in the shoulder or the extension on the belly in the area of the hips, because the intestines descend from this rupture to one of the kidneys; and this rupture is in the shoulder or from the extension of it, and these two manners come from many causes: from a blow, or a jump, or a fall, or lifting heavy weights, and similar things; and the sign when it is from the extension of the shoulder is that it happens little by little, over a long time, and does not come suddenly; and the abscess is equal up to near the bottom, because the shoulder presses on the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	 And the sign is when it comes from the section of the hip, which brings sudden pain at the beginning, and the abscess has a diverse appearance, beneath the skin near, and this is due to the exit of the intestines and the body lacking in the hip area.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	 And sometimes the coils come out with the intestines and are retained within, causing great pain for the patient, especially when they are pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	 And in these cures by iron, there is fear, so one must avoid them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	 And the manner of the work is such that you instruct the patient to put his intestine back into his hand inside the wound if it can go in; then have him sit up on his knees between your hands, and raise his thighs; then straighten the heart above, and cut all the skin of the testicles lengthwise; then insert the fingers of the waist uncinate as needed to open the wound, and let it be such that the intestines can come out; then remove the hip that is under the skin of the testicles until the white hip bone is uncovered on all sides; then put your index finger in that which follows the testicle, in that which is between the white hip bone that is under the skin of the egg, and between the second hip bone, and separate that which is behind the egg, and between the second hip bone; and then move to the right hand inside the heart of the testicles, and straighten the white hip bone up to your left hand, and raise the egg with all the hip bones towards the waist; and instruct the assistant to extend the egg upwards, and release that which is tied behind the bandage;
