and check with your fingers if there is any intestine wrapped in the hard white hip bone, and if you find anything, put it back into the abdomen below; then take a needle with a thread made of X threads thick, and put it in the rear part of the hip bone that is after the skin of the testicles, after the waist, then cut the heads that appear from the threads until there are IV threads; then assemble them one on top of the other in the shape of a cross, and bind the hip bone, which we have said is under the skin of the testicles, with a strong bandage of II parts; then wrap the heads of the threads, and tie them firmly with II parts, so that none of the servants who nurse them can enter into it, where no such abscess will come; and put again the bandage according to the first long bandage of II fingers from that, and after these II bandages leave the hip bone under the heart of the testicles the width of a finger; and after all the other according to the roundness that the egg carries; then cut in the part that is under the skin of the testicles until the veins run, and swell, as we have said above; then bring moist wool in oil, and put it in the wounds, and bring the bandage that we have mentioned.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	 And sometimes the white part is cauterized as we have said, after the incision, out of fear of blood loss.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	 For this happens many times, and let the pus drain on its own; and if it delays in draining, then it should be washed with hot water, and put on what we have said, until it drains; then treat the wound with another treatment, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	 of flesh hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	 In this ramus, I have never seen anyone who dared to make the cure with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And the ancients said that it is done like the ramus which is with the sinew, in such a way that you tie the vessels, after cutting above lightly below; then cut in half, and treat the abscess as we have said, until the vessel drains; and treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	 Some times comes a rupture in the anus, as we have said, and opens the place; and no one should touch the intestines in the belly, and if they do touch them, it is not good, and it repairs every hour; but nevertheless if it lingers too long in this state, then the wound or swelling grows until the intestines come out; and this happens due to the expansion of the swelling that is in the anus, as we have said, for it expands, then the place becomes soft and inflamed and open; and the cure is by cautery, as we have previously said; sometimes it is cured with iron in this manner: and it is that the patient lies on their back between your hands, then cut the swelling of the rupture from its width according to the size of three fingers; and then remove the swelling that is under the skin like the others, then take a needle and place it on the visible part of the swelling; and press it deeply into the belly, then sew the two visible parts of the swelling onto the head of the needle, and sew one and the other; then remove the head of the needle, and do not cut into the swelling or expand the egg or anything else, as I have taught you in the cure of the rupture of the intestines; then treat it with the treatment for wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 And when you cut the threads, so cleanse and treat the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	 The silk is tight, and has no appearance in the suture, and the cautery is more effective in this place, and closer to health.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	 of the softening of the skin of the testicles
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	 Often the skin of the testicles is softened in some men because the glands inside are softened, and it can be seen as pus; and it is necessary that when one wants to treat it, one should make the patient lie on his back, and cut the softened skin onto the natural skin; then join the two lips with a suture, and if you wish, first sew the superfluous part of the softened skin with three or four stitches firmly; then cut between the stitches, and treat it like other wounds until it is healed, and the threads fall out. xspace
dou chastrement	 For the incision
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	 Know that incision is forbidden in our law, and therefore it pleases me not to speak of it in this book; it is only necessary for two reasons: one is that the physician knows how to respond when asked, and knows how to perform the treatment; the other reason is that we often have need of incising certain animals to help us, such as goats, sheep, and dogs and other animals.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	 I say therefore that incision is done in two ways: by attraction or by division.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	 In the method that we perform by attraction, we make the animal sit in hot water until the ligaments are softened and hanging; then take them with your hand, replacing them until you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 Of castration of the tail: it is necessary that you tie the beast and press the skin of its testicles with your left hand, then bind the suspensory ligament, and cut above each testicle with one cut, when you have well exposed them; and leave a small pocket of fat and the subtle fat that is on the vessels; and this manner of castration is more effective than that done by attraction, because in attraction sometimes something remains of the testicles, which makes the beast desire lust; then treat the wound until it heals.
des hermofrodites	 of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	 The first manner of hermaphrodite in men is that between the two testicles appears like the natural form of a woman, where there is hair, and sometimes urine flows from it.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	 And the other method is for women, and it is placed on the wrist like a rod and two cubits long.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	 And the treatment for both man and woman is that you cut all the cartilage pieces, and treat them as other wounds; in the second method, of men whose urine passes through the skin of the testicles, there is no treatment.
de la tentigene	 Of the fever
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	 Fever is a cartilage on the natural part, which is so ugly to see; and some women have it as large as a hand, and this is the treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	 It is necessary that you remove the superfluity of the fever to your hand or nails, and cut it lightly; and do not go too deep, lest blood come out, then treat it with other treatment until it is healed; and another cartilage that appears at the mouth of the womb, and fills it, and by chance goes strong, and it resembles a cow's head, and for this reason the ancients called it "cow disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	 If it is necessary, you must cut it off, as we have said about the tendon, and treat it until it heals.
de erratique	 of error
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	 Erratic it is when the woman's nature is not understood, or the opening is small; and it is natural by birth, or accidental due to illness that has come about; or it is caused by improper union, or by a subtle or thick humor, and is made deep in the womb, or on the side, or below, wherever it may be; and it prevents conception, childbirth, and possibly menstruation; and knowledge of this comes from observing the urine.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	 If the swelling is imminent, it will appear at your thumb or foot.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	 S'il est du syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, and let the woman be on her back, spreading her legs; then stretch the II leivres firmly, so that the subtil syfac is round, and there should be an obstruction; then take wool, and moisten it in oil, and place it on the spot, and have the woman lie down every day, so that it cannot heal.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	 And if the syfac is hard and thick, you should cut it with a spatula similar to a myrtle leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the obstruction is of fresh flesh, suspend it with onion and cut it; and have hemostatic medicines, such as acacia, dragon's blood, incense, abundantly mixed with egg; then apply a wide sheet of lead, so that the wound cannot heal; and thus let it be for a long time, and apply a tent of dry linen; then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	 And when in the flesh comes a boil, it must be covered in this manner, if it is not an infected abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	 For an infected abscess that is in the flesh, one should not touch or make with fire.
des emorroides	 of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	 Hemorrhoids are openings of veins which without skin usually appear, and when hemorrhoids are old they become hard; and we have said in the division their similarities and signs, and I will say here those which receive treatment.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	 I say that hemorrhoids and hardened ones, when they are deeply embedded in the flesh and do not appear to the touch, are not cured by fire.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	 Those who are at the edge of death, which can be felt, are those whom one can cure.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	 It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold house; then place the altelul in tongs, and cut its roots, then sprinkle on restricting blood medicines, such as acacia and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then soak her feet against the wall for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if blood continues to flow, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate bark and galls and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and oil, and make a plaster on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	 And if it bleeds, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	 If not, then apply cupping glasses to the back and breasts without cutting; then take wool, and soak it in juice of plantain or juice of hawthorn with old wine, and apply to the place.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when the abscess subsides, then treat the place with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a rough head, which must be covered as I have said above; and then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	 of the abscesses of the uterus
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	 Many types of abscess occur in the uterus, such as canker, purulent abscess, herpes, cysts, fistulas, hemorrhoids, and hot abscess, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	 It is therefore necessary that in this treatise I speak of the hot abscess that comes in the thigh, which is not one of those that swell well; and if you wish to know the work of fire, look at whether the abscess is sharp at the beginning of its appearance, and full of heat and fever, and whether it turns red if you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	 Then do not hasten to pierce, but let the abscess mature until the pain is relieved; and then have the patient sit on a chair, and let there be two small chairs where he can lean back, and support his back and bring together his feet at the parts beyond the thigh; and let his thighs be spread out, and let him place his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a good ligature; then give him to drink towards the left side, and bring to him the instrument with which one works the opening of the thigh, of which comes later the form; and it is necessary that when you see this instrument brought to him, that you first insert the tip to know the depth of the thigh, so that what enters from the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and does not harm the patient; and if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the thigh with cloths, so that the instrument does not harm him; and it is necessary that he place the horn of the instrument above, and let the instrument be heated.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	 And when the abscess opens, and one makes an incision in the soft hand, it must be covered at the top with white leek; and when the boil is emptied, it is necessary to put in the wound bandages moistened in rose oil, or in dry green oil; and place the bandage on the outside of the wound at the bottom of the cloth, and place on top of the cloth and on the pillow a clean wet linen sheet soaked in water or mallows, cooked; then cure after two days of ointment, according to this, until it is healed; and sometimes raise the boil and the wound with an enema of water and honey, and then of water with lily roots and long aristolochia, cooked; then return to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	 Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.
de l’enfantement	 of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	 Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, and the second follows with it.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	 Car it happens sometimes on his feet, and comes on the body or the head, or the hands, where it appears on the stomach, or sometimes, and is transformed by chance onto his neck, and in other malevolent forms; thus it is necessary for the nurse that she be wise and skillful in these things, and guard against error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one should assist her.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	 If the child comes out on his head by natural birth, and the woman gives birth painfully, and her strength is weak, then have her sit on a stool, where women hold her; and let her nature come down with oil or fenugreek that has been cooked, and then the nurse puts between her teeth the small spatula whose form is thus:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	 And split the secondine, and cut to its nail so that the moisture inside runs out; and press on the woman's belly until the child descends, and if it does not descend, then one must enema the woman with a muslin bag of fenugreek with sesame oil; then make her press and sneeze condiments, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: thus the child will be expelled now.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	 And if the two hands come out forcefully, then you must gently push them back little by little; and if they cannot go in, put the woman on a stool, and lift her feet up high; then knock over the stool onto the ground, and hold the woman so she does not fall during this process; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child dies, cut the hands with the knife that was placed before, and extract the child, and also reset.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	 of the child's exit onto its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	 When the child comes onto its feet, you should push it upwards; and then turn it little by little until it is level; then take hold of one of the feet and extend it little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	 When he jumps up to his knees, instruct him to sneeze forcefully, and then jump higher, if God wills it.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	 And if he does not jump as high as we have said, then turn him little by little until he is according to the natural figure.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	 Because then he will be light.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	 And if he does not come as high as we have said, take althea powder, and oil of sesame, and melted gum, and grind all in a mortar; and apply this ointment to the woman’s natural place, both inside and outside; then let her sit in hot water up to her ribs; and when she is sufficiently soaked, give her a mixture of myrrh, and put it under her, and leave it for an hour; then let her sit on a stool, then make her sneeze and hold her mouth and nose, and lightly grasp her belly, because the child will now jump.  (Note: The word "naturel" can also mean "natural place," i.e., the vagina.)
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	 Of the delivery of the child upon its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	 When the child comes in this form, let the midwife put her hands little by little; then she should be supported on its neck, and the feet should hang down, and it should lie on the bed; and fold its hands little by little, and then take the hands above the belly, and remove the cushions below, until it is prepared to descend; and if the child does not jump, take its feet and move them forcefully, then move the belly up, then put your hands in; and pull the child little by little; and instruct the woman to hold on until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	 Of the delivery of the child that comes with one hand hanging down
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	 It is necessary to contrive to bring back the hand: if it cannot be brought back, then make the woman get up and walk; if she cannot walk, then make her lie on the bed, and prop up her legs very well; then introduce the mustard poultice that I have mentioned; and if she does not give birth, then make her sit on a chair, then study to bring back the hand; and examine the child according to its natural form, and make it sneeze, and instruct her to hold on until the child comes out.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	 of the emergence of the child from its neck, and its hands extended, and its face turned towards the back of its mother
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	 It is necessary that the midwife take her hand, then turn it little by little, and examine it lightly; and when it is equal, place on top the natural mustard poultice of althaea and oil, as we have said, then instruct her to move little by little; and when you have done this, make her sit on a chair, and instruct her to hold on; and make her sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	 In this same manner, for all the second stage
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	 When it comes out with force in this manner for all the second stage, then cut the second stage with your fingernail until the moisture is emptied; and if the child turns on its face and on its neck, then cut from below, so that it is not held back, and let the child die; then push the child inside until you have placed him as he should be, and command the woman to take herself some time: then it will come out easily.
de l’issue des gemelz	 of the birth of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	 Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four are born; and this is not a strange thing, and happens rarely.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	 Two are strange and do not live, if at all; I know that they are multiparous, and are divided by the siphac that separates them, which is attached to the bottom; and sometimes they come out as naturally as one alone, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	 And if they come out violently, then treat it as we have said, and let the bandage be subtle, and act quickly and lightly as she does; and act thus as he is moved to safety.
de plusors enfans	 of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	 Sometimes they are formed in the womb as one or two or three or four or five or six or seven, or even more up to fifteen, and all are fully formed in the shape of a child according to the wise and glorious measure. And it is necessary that the bandage knows all these things, for perhaps similar things may happen; thus act accordingly as is needed.
de l’enfant mort	 of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	 When you treat the woman for the dead child in her womb, as I have said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are forced to work with your hands; then it is necessary that you know if the woman is of healthy virtue, and has no accident where she fears death. Then let the woman be laid on her back, and let her head hang downwards, and let her legs be raised; and the servant brings the needle in two parts, where she lies in bed so that she may not be pulled down by the child's descent. Then rub the mouth of the womb with moistened oils, with a cloth of althea and fenugreek and linseed, then anoint the bandage’s hands with these oils and these cloths; then they put them lightly into the womb, then seek one place where she puts the needles that are suitable for this, and take care if the child is prepared to descend onto its head; then stick the needles in his eyes or in his neck or in his mouth or in some of his palate or under his beard or in his stomach or near his sides, and if the descent is on the feet, then stick it in the fist and in the middle of the ribs. And it is necessary that he holds the needle with his right hand, and places the thumb between his left-hand fingers, and puts all his hand lightly, and sticks the needle in any of these places that we have said, until it reaches the empty thing; and this is the shape of the needle:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	 Then push against the other bone, or a third if you need it, so that the extraction is equal; and then hold them equally while moving from one side to the other, so that it may come out, and let the bones be interlocked to keep it in place, as shown here in this form:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	 And if a part remains, then apply some of the oil from his finger to that part and draw out the other part; and if nothing remains, place this bone in a higher position, and repeat until it all comes out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	 And if one hand comes before the other and cannot be brought back due to constriction, then you must wrap it in a cloth until it all comes out; then cut off at the joint of the foot or the thigh, and so you should do with the other hand and both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	 And if the child's head is large and it is stuck in the birth canal, or if there is a sharp bone assembled at the top, then you must insert the thorny spatula between your teeth and pierce the skull and extract the bone; or you can use the instrument called "almidach," from which the shape comes with the instruments in the following chapter; and do the same if the child has a large natural head. Then draw out the bones with the forceps, and if the head is still stuck and it is held by the membrane, then split it until the moisture that is in the worst part can come out. And if it cannot come out, then break it into pieces as much as you can; and if the belly or ribs are swollen, then you must pierce until the moisture flows out.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	 And if the child is on its feet, then the traction is light, and the application to the mother's mouth is easy.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	 And if it is prolapsed into the belly or the breast, then you must pull it out wrapped in a cloth on your hand; and open the belly or the breast, until the moisture inside is corrected; and if the other members are removed, and the head remains, then the midwife should insert her hand deep into the mother's vagina, and draw it up to the mother's mouth; then she should put in one or two ounces of oil, and draw harder; and if the mother's vagina is narrow due to a hot abscess that has occurred there, then one must not struggle, but rather administer moist and greasy things; and the administrator should apply poultices, and wash with softening and moistening water.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	 Et si l'enfant est sur son côté, et tu peux le mettre en ligne droite, alors procède comme nous avons dit pour l'enfant vivant; et s'il n'y a pas de pouvoir, alors perce-le par morceaux, et ne laisse rien de la seconde.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	 Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li mestier est comme nous avons dit dans les abcès qui viennent sur la chair; et s'il y a un écoulement de sang, alors mets-y une ligature serrée, et fais d'autres soins.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	 And I saw a woman in whose womb one child had died, and then another was conceived on top of it, and that other also died.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	 After a long time, he developed an abscess on the thigh, which swelled until it burst, and began to exude greatly.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	 I was called to treat it, and thought about it for a long time, but the wound could not be healed.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	 I applied a strong drawing plaster, and from it came out a bone, and after some days another one.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	 I was greatly amazed, for the belly has no bones at all.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	 So I thought that these were the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	 I cleaned the wound and removed many bones until the woman was in better condition; and the woman lived for a long time thus, and always exuded a little pus from that place; and I have remembered this chapter only because, when the master finds something strange, he should know how to handle it.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	 to bring the wound back to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	 Here comes the form of the press, which one makes according to the books; and at two turns are the two keys of the two straps.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	 Nevertheless, the horns should be more subtle than the straps, and should be made of boxwood or ebony; and the mouth of the wooden cylinder should be two fingers wide, and the edge of the tree one finger, and in length one palm and a half; and between the two straps there should be two pieces of this same wood, which are fixed in one and the other, half a palm long or a little more; and these two pieces are pushed into the mouth of the wound to open when one turns the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	 One other form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, made of ebony or boxwood according to the appearance of tongs; and at its two ends, let there be two adjustments, as you see, one palm long and two fingers wide; and when you see opening the vulva with the entire instrument, make the woman sit on a bed, her feet hanging and her legs open, then place the two adjustments close together in the vulva, and hold the head of the instrument under between her thighs; then work your hand with the entire instrument, as you have done with the tongs equally, according to the width that you see opening the mouth of the vulva, so much that the vagina does what it wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	 This instrument is all prepared, and their likenesses are multiplied; and when the surgeon has them ready, the work is more urgent, and higher for men by their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	 Do not discard the instrument until you have prepared it, for their needs are not negligible.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	 When the umbilical cord is caught during childbirth, you must instruct the patient to hold her breath, then make her sneeze strongly, and hold your hands over her mouth and nose; and if it comes out this way, all is well.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	 If not, take a pot and make a hole in the lid, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the womb, such as calamint, rue, anise, chamomile, cinnamon and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, be cooked in the pot with water over the fire; then put a reed through the hole in the pot, and the other end in the mouth of the woman, and hold it until the vapor enters the womb; then make her sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	 If the ligament is cut quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	 And if it remains after this treatment, and is not strong, then instruct the patient to moisten her left hand in sesame oil or musk-scented water, and then insert it into the vagina, and seek the ligament; and when she has found it, she should take it and gently stretch it little by little straightly, so that the cervix does not prolapse during extraction; but it must be moved lightly to the right and left, and then pull; it will come out and desiccate.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	 And if the mouth of the uterus is tightly closed, we have said the cure of sneezing and fumigation with herbs; and if it does not come from any of these things that we have said, then be careful not to rush when pulling; but you must tie what is at the mouth of the uterus to the thigh of the woman, then give an enema with the compound of four drugs; thus it will decay and return, and become strong; but nevertheless, when it decays, bad odor comes to the stomach and head, and harms the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	 If it is necessary, then proper fumigations are required for this: some of the ancients have proven the fumigation of watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	 The form of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman to retain the flow and the afterbirth is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	 And it is made of glass like a jug, and one places the fine end in the vagina, and the wide ends over the fire; and let the fumigation be on the coals, and continue until it is consumed, and then start another one.
de percier lou fondement	 to pierce the anus
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Many children are born whose anus is not pierced, but rather is closed by a thin membrane: it is therefore necessary for the midwife to pierce this membrane with her finger, and not with a sharp spatula, and she should take care that she does not touch it; then place on moistened linen in wine and oil, then the cure of anointing until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	 And if you doubt that it will not stop, then put a piece of lead in the hole and leave it for less days, and let it be removed when the child wants to go into rooms.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	 And sometimes this stoppage comes from the sudden occurrence of a wound or abscess; then it is necessary to cover that sudden occurrence: and let it be treated as we have said about the piece of lead.
de la fistule dou fondement	 about the fistula of the anus
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	 Fistulas that come from under the anus are nodules, and those that come from beside the anus outward, or in the space of the two parts, if there is one fistula or more; and when this nodule is old, it works, and increases moisture with white or subtle boil, and sometimes these fistulas are persistent; and they are known by this, that during egestion or ventosity when the patient has egestion, and perhaps one of them goes out.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	 Et si a fistules that perforate up to the bladder, and up to half of the penis; and they reach up to the hip joint, and up to the knee socket.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	 And thus one knows the fistula perforating the anus, and not perforating: and it is that you place your finger in the anus, and insert a fine needle of iron or steel into the fistula when there is no tortuosity.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	 And if there is tortuosity, then you insert a fine leaden thread, or a horsehair, so that you feel the thread or hair with your finger; and if you do not feel it, and no excretion, gas, or feces come out of the opening as we have said: know that it does not perforate; then hasten to cure it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	 Et when the fistula extends to the bladder or to the passage of the urine, then the urine leaks out, and it cannot be healed by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	 If it is perforated to the point of the hip, then the bag comes up to that place; but if there is a twist and the cause of the pain around it, it is that it will always protrude, and neither medicine nor ointment for healing is effective; and in these perforating fistulas there is no cure except labor, and foolish physicians waste their time on them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	 In the one that is not perforating and is not old, there is hope of healing with iron, as I have experienced; and it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and he lifts his legs up to his thighs, and has his thighs inclined towards his belly; then insert a probe of bronze, or of lead if there is tortuosity, until you know where the bag comes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	 If the patient feels it around the anus, then you must insert your finger into it, and if you feel that the tent has been perforated; and it is exposed where you sense between your finger the sinew or flesh, then know that it is perished, so do not waste time trying to heal it.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	 However, it is said that one can heal some well, but this happens rarely; and the aid that is done is to heat the subtle cautery according to the width of the fistula, as was said before; and insert it all hot into the fistula, until it reaches near the anus; and do this two or three times, so that you know those fleshy parts are burned, which are like a feather of a bird; and then cure the wet tent with butter, so that this flesh comes out, then cure the wound by applying greasy flesh and suturing.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	 If he is thus healed, that is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	 If he cannot be healed otherwise; and if the fistula enters, but does not perforate up to the finger that is in the base, and there is a thick layer of flesh or silk between your finger and the fistula, and you see the fistula at the edge of this cover; then cut off from the beginning of the fistula, and push the probe forward always, and afterwards cauterize, until it reaches the tip of the fistula; and the fistula will be freed and will fall out; then cleanse those fleshy growths that resemble a bird's feather, and nothing should remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	 And if the pus overcomes you and enters between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or strong medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	 Car the fire cautery accomplishes two good things: that is to say, the burning of these hairs nearby, and the stopping of blood and the drying out of moisture; then cure moist tents in butter or in crushed things, until the place throws off the pus, and the burned hair emerges from the pus; then treat the wound with hardening ointments made from dry herbs, and these medicines are dry.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	 When it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	 And if the fistula reaches to the bottom of the anus and is distant from the body, then press your finger into the anus and inquire about it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	 If you feel the tent and between the two there is cloth or silk or hair, or it is near to perforating, do not despair, for there are three ways of treatment: either you cauterize as we have said, or you cut until the bottom, or if you can, place tents and treat as before; and do not go too deep, lest you cut the structure that holds the anus, and uncontrolled defecation occurs; then treat as we have said; perhaps it will be healed, or remove that covering and clean it after it has been cut near the anus, either by tent or by other suitable instrument; then clean the hairy flesh in the wound as much as you can; then strive to restore the wound, and to prevent the fistula from returning to the part below the anus: this will be a lighter task for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	 And sometimes there are fistulas in this manner: and when you insert the tent into the fistula, which is on the side of the anus near the skin above, then take a tent pierced at the tip according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	 And insert a twisted thread into it, and insert the tent with all the thread into the fistula until it reaches the tip.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	 If it is perforating the margin of the anus within, then extract the thread from that hole, so that you insert your finger into the anus; and draw out the tip of the thread, and join the two tips together, and hold them together, and leave it for one day or two; and restrain it sometimes, until the thread cuts those parts which are between the two, and they fall off; then treat the wound until it is healed and cured.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	 Si la fistule ne perce pas, fais-la percer de toutes les manières possibles, sauf si elle est trop profonde.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 For it is not fitting to cover the wound too deeply with a cap, and then heal it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	 The shape of the pointed spatula used to make the fistula is very sharp on one side and cutting; and on the other side it is not, so that you do not cover what should not be covered, as you can see here:
des emorroydes	 from hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	 Hemorrhoids are of two types: either they are inside the anus like a resin grain, and there may be small or large ones, and blood always comes out with them, and there may be one or several, and they are outside the anus and at the edge of the anus; but those that are outside have little moisture, and sometimes come out with a little citrus water or a little blood, and have the color of the flesh; and the cure for those who have them inside the anus is that you instruct the patient to squeeze to defecate in the chambers until the anus comes out, and the threads appear; then hurry, and hold it with tweezers, or with your nail, then cut at its roots; and if the nails cannot hold them because of their moisture, take them with a piece of cloth, or cotton, or a piece of camlet; and pull them with your fingers, then cut them, and sprinkle on top some hot powders that serve as cautery; or cauterize them as it is said in the chapter on cautery, then cure with other cures until they are healed; and if the anus cannot come out, make the patient take a laxative enema that is biting and harsh to wash what is in the anus so that it can come out clearly; when the patient squeezes, and the threads come out of the anus, the cure is light; and it is that you hold them with your nail or tweezers, and cut them, then cure as we have said until they are healed, and beware of incision by iron. ›
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere:
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	 Of dryness of the intestines or rectum
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	 Many times there is dryness in the intestines, due to natural constraint, and when the illness is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then you should scrape the surface of the skin with a spatula or your fingernail, so that it does not moisten; then treat it until it is dry as needed; and if it cannot be dried, then start scraping again stronger than before, until it bleeds profusely and becomes raw; then treat it until it heals.
dou fremit	 Of trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	 Ants are small creatures that crawl over the body and go very deeply; sometimes they feel cold, and one feels it like a chill, and it spreads throughout the body, more in the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	 And the cure is such that you take a reed from a goose feather, or a strong bird feather, and place that reed on the tremor, until the circle of purple reaches all around the tremor; then turn your hand with all the reed so that you encircle all around the tremor, and put it in deeply, and extract the tremor from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	 And if you see, do this with a reed of brass or iron according to this form, and let it be subtle below and drawn above:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	 not at all piercing, in order to hold the two together and press them, And if you see, then cauterize the tremor, just as it is stated in the chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	 of the form of the enema
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	 Sometimes one makes an enema of silver or gold, or of melted bronze or iron; and sometimes one makes these instruments in small and large sizes, according to those for whom they are prepared.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	 Therefore, those who are prepared for the treatment of children and who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	 The form of the small and large enema is wide at the top, where the intestines are tied in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	 and there should be an opening where the intestines are tied as you see, and the end is pierced; and on one side there should be two holes, and on the other one; and let the intestine in which the medicines are placed be of the bladder of a beast or of parchment, and it should be pierced all around with small holes, and between each hole there should be one finger's breadth, then put a strong thread through these holes, twisted like an X or twisted around, and gather the intestine as if it were a goatskin; and when the medicine is inside, tie it to the instrument in front with a strong thread, then give the enema; and this is the form of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	 And let the medicine not be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head of the enema with oil or egg yolk, or similar substance, then insert it gently; then the minister should press with both hands together until all is expelled, then remove the enema, and have the patient lift his legs to the wall, and if the medicine wants to come out, hold it as long as possible; and if he sleeps through the night, it is of greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if you enema him for a disease of the swollen belly, and the medicine hastens to come out, then repeat it until he is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	 And if there are hemorrhoids or an abscess in the rectum, then let the enema be as fine as for a child; and this is the form of the fine enema, on which the skin should be pulled taut:
des plaies	 of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	 We have said in the division the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you about the treatments of hands and medicine according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	 I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and what they are made of.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	 The things by which wounds are made are by the striking of a stone, and cutting with a sword or knife, or a lance or stick or arrow, or similar things; or they are made according to the places on the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or the head, or the foot, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members. And I will tell you the treatment of each wound, and I will begin with simple wounds of the head, for the reminder will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	 I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, take care if it is from the fall of a stone or similar things, and the skin is nevertheless torn and the wound is large, and you suspect a hot abscess: then bleed it immediately with the cephalic vein itself if little blood comes from the wound, and let the bleeding be opposite to the affected part; and the patient should avoid overeating wine and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if he does not want to bleed, let his food be reduced, and let him drink no wine, nor eat meat; and put on the wound, if hot abscesses come there, cotton soaked only in rose oil or stiptic wine; and if there is no hot abscess, put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and not moved by the air, a powder that I will say a little later; and if the air has moved it, put on some ointments until he is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	 And if the wound is large like a sword cut and similar, and the lips cannot be brought together by stitches, then bring them together by sewing, as I will say for wounds of the belly, with the seam.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	 If the wound is exposed to the bone and deep, and only holds by a tuft, then shave it; then cure the wound with medicine, and replace hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat coarse foods, such as bread and cooked meat, also like pulses, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	 And if you find that there is rotting in the skin and it reaches to the bone, then cut away all the rot, and throw it away, then cure it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein which cannot be stopped by medicines, then seek the artery, and if you find it dislocated, then tie it with a thread; and if this does not help at all, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	 And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: and it is that you put in this powder that heals before the fire has moved it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 And the manner of the powder is this: take one part of incense; two parts of dragon's blood; three parts of quicklime, and make it into a fine powder. Fill the wound with it and bind it tightly until it dries well and adheres to all its flesh; then bandage it well and leave it unwrapped if it does not swell, for one should not remove the medicine until it is healed.
