Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	 And sometimes one does this with only quicklime, when one does not have incense or dragon's blood, but the fire has moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the fire has moved the wound, even so, do not put this powder on it; but put some cooked onions, or poultices of barley flour made with water and honey, until it casts out pus; then continue other cures until he is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	 And if the fracture of bone comes with the wound, and it is small, draw it out with fine forceps; and I will tell you hereafter about the fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	 of a neck wound
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	 If the wound is in the neck and it is simple, then there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the sinew of the neck or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	 If it is the nerve, then there is no other remedy than to leave the wound alone and not apply anything that might constrict it, for this harms the nerves and causes them to retreat; and do not put anything cold on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member; but let the medicine be warm, like warm water mixed with rose oil, and wash the wound in such warm water, and other stones or herbs according to this method, and moist dressings.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the wound is large, stitch it up and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it heals.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	 And if the wounds are deep and the blood vessel is cut and full of blood, then open it in a lower place; and if the artery is cut and blood flows out, then expose it, and let it bleed, and cauterize it if necessary; and if the windpipe is cut, or the heart, and the passage is blocked so that the meat does not pass, then sew up the windpipe on the skin of the neck, and do not touch the throat but put it back according to its natural shape; and then bind it properly, and leave it for some days, then treat it with dry dressings until it heals; and if the wound has affected the bone, then open it; and if there are pieces of bone, then draw them out completely if you can, and those that you cannot have, leave them until the wound becomes putrid, and the issue is clear and clean; and if the wound is fresh, then powder on the powder that I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	 And if there are bones in the wound and it has an abscess, then treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	 of the spear or dagger wound
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	 If it is a spear or dagger wound and the wound is deep, observe if there is gas from the wound when the patient breathes: know then that the wound is mortal. And if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, do not put powder on it in the first hour, nor tie it so that the blood does not drain deeply, but returns to the heart, and kills the patient; but apply a drawing ointment, and bind it twice a day. And if you do not have an ointment, put old cotton in the wound to absorb the moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four, or more; thus no spasm, no bad tremor of the heart, nor breathing difficulties will occur. And when you see good signs, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	 Cure it then with poultices and other dressings until it is healed; and if it cannot heal, and festers, know that there is a fistula; treat it as you should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	 And if the wound is from the cutting of a sword or knife, and it is simple, either in the flesh or in the back, then treat it like those in front; if it is large, with stitching; and if it is small, with powder, and if it has struck near the bone and has shattered pieces, then seek out the wound, and remove the fragments if they are exposed; and if they are not exposed, let the wound fester, which will ease the extraction; and for other wounds in other limbs, the treatment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	 From the rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	 The rupture of the belly is great and medium and small; from the large wound sometimes the intestines or the nerves of the intestines protrude, which causes their protrusion; and the suture is more difficult, and sometimes the small wound is worse than the large one, because one can put back the intestines less easily, unless they are put back little by little; because the intestine swells as soon as it feels the cold, it goes back less easily, and therefore the medium wound is better, because one puts back the intestine more easily to its place than in the others. And know that the rupture of the belly is according to four ways: the two common sutures happen in the suture of the belly, and the suture of the other wounds of the body, and the two other proper sutures are common with the other wounds; nevertheless, they are more specific with the suture of the belly, and I will say each one and explain.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	 Je dis que quand la plaie est petite, et quelque chose de l'intestin sort par force, c'est une chose difficile à remettre, cela se fait par l'une des deux manières : soit en raison de la petitesse de la plaie, comme nous l'avons dit, soit parce que l'intestin est gonflé par le froid.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	 Et quand il est froid, réchauffez-le de la manière suivante : mouillez une éponge ou un léger linge avec seulement de l'eau tiède, ou cuisez dans de l'eau avec du cumin et du fenouil, et arrosez l'intestin jusqu'à ce que le gonflement soit retiré; parfois, ce vin a un effet resserrant, et il est plus sûr d'utiliser seulement pour désenfler.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	 And when you see the swelling subside, then moisten the intestine with hot water or wine and it should be cooked well, because through this it is made easier to enter by a small amount; and if it cannot enter, then make a small incision in the wound with an instrument for cutting hemorrhoids; and the first care is to make sure that the cutter cuts, for no one should cut without great necessity being present; and this is the instrument to split it: then cut inside the curve and not outside, and see here the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	 And when the wound is widened, and the intestine jumps out, then place it back in its natural form in its proper place, if you can, because this is worth more.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	 When the wound is wide and it is in the part below the belly, then you must make the patient lie on his back, and put his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the part below the belly, then put the head and the feet higher than the parts below, and so also if the rupture of the belly is in one of the two parts, put your attention to it so that the wounded part may be higher than the other; and thus you must administer this for large and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	 In small wounds put what you have prepared, then have between your hands a skillful servant who may hold all the rupture in his hand, and bring together the lips; and this is the common manner of sutures, which is that you take one or more needles according to the width of the wound, then leave two fingers' width from the head of the wound, and put a needle where there is a strong good thread; and pierce the two heads of the skin with the two heads of the siphac, which is under the skin inside, so much that you make it pierce through this part, and bring together the two heads of the siphac four together; then strain a double thread around the needle in two parts, then bring together the two lips of the wound suitably, and then leave two fingers' width, and put another needle; then tie the thread as you did the first needle, and do not cease doing this according to what you need for the needles, until all the wound is restrained; and let the needles be medium, between subtle and thick, because subtle needles cut all the flesh, and too thick ones cannot enter well: therefore they must be medium; and it is not necessary to push the needles too far into the flesh and skin, that they may not cut and work the wound before the suture; and then cut the heads of the needles so that they do not hurt the patient while sleeping, and put caps or bandages on the heads of the needles to keep them in place, and leave them until the wound is healed; and this manner of suture with needles is more convenient for small wounds, because one can fit an additional needle or two in the second suture, which is common, which is that you bring together the two heads of the skin and the two heads of the siphac together at a needle where there is a strong medium thread; and when you have pierced these four heads together, then remove the needle to the part where you began, in the manner that clothes are sewn; and put space between each suture as thick as a small finger; this suture is known by men, and I sewed a wound that a man had in the belly, which was cut with a knife, and the wound was more than one palm wide, and the intestines protruded two palms' width, and the wound was in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	 I returned the intestines to him after they had been out for twenty-four hours, and the wound was closed until fifteen days, and I cared for it, and he was healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	 And the doctors had judged that he would die, and this was a miracle; and I did not treat him with ointment, because I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicines; and I put old cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until he was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	 Now I will tell you the two proper methods of suturing: take the needle and pass it from the outside to the inside; when it has pierced the skin straight on, let the head of the thread or stitch rest where you have passed the needle, and make it come out on the other side from the inside to the outside; and the intention of this suturing is that you sew just as furriers sew furs, leaving the thread once on one side and taking it again on the other, until the suture is completely done.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	 The second method of stitching, which Galen specifically mentions, is done as some people do, who naturally bring together the two parts and apply one of the ends of the silk to the other end, in such a manner: stick a needle into the end of the silk near it, and make it pierce that place only, and leave the two ends of the silk; then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the outer part until it reaches the inner one, at the two ends of the silk; then make it pierce one and the other from the outer part until it reaches the inner one, in two other places of the silk that are on either side; and this is the milder method of stitching and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	 Galiens thus said these words, and some testify to it, that one must sew the belly with two needles, having thread in each; and one should insert one needle from one side, and the other from the opposite side, in the manner of those who make belts; and know that when the suture is in the middle of the belly, the stitching is greater than in other places of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	 The judgment of the wound is such as the judgment of other wounds: and it is that when you find the fresh wound all its blood, before the fire has moved it, then reset the intestine and the seam; then put on a powder with flesh-healing herbs, and if the fire has moved it, then put on some ointment that is present, until the wound swells; and stitch the silk thread, and let the sifac and mirach be bound; then cure the wound as the others, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicines, then put on, as soon as it begins to throw pus, old cotton, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	 Car you do not need any other medicine in many cases when the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound may spread to the main members, then it is necessary that you moisten a light linen cloth in warm oil or rose oil, and place it around the joints and under the armpits; and if he feels pain or putrefaction in his bowels, and this often happens, then give him an enema of tepid black wine, and likewise if the putrefaction extends to the intestines; and pierce it from within, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	 The intestine which is called "jeun" cannot heal when it is wounded, and this is due to the thinness of the veins that are there, and due to the subtlety of the whole body, and the proximity of its nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	 And if the intestine protrudes from the wound, put it back like the intestines while it is fresh; and if it is old and turned green or black, then you must tie the black part so that no blood flows there, for there are veins and arteries; then cut what is between the ties, and hang the two ends from the lower part of the wound until it falls out, and the wound closes.
de la routure dou boueil	 of the bursting of a boil
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	 When the intestine is rent, and the wound is small, then it can be restored in some men, for I saw that a man was wounded in the belly by a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it swelled and became fistulous, and from it issued pus and windiness; I applied a cure according to what I could, and did not cease to refine until he was healthy, and the place healed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	 And when I saw it soldered, I feared that the patient might have an ailment in his belly; but there was no ailment, and he remained in better condition, eating and drinking; and some experts said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be tied in this manner: take large-headed pins, then bring together the lips of the wound, and when the pin has opened its mouth, place it on the two lips so that it closes its mouth upon them; and then cut off the head, and this holds so that it cannot become undone, then place another pin after in the same manner as before, until the wound is completely surrounded; and sew up the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	 When the heads of these [things] settle in the intestines, and no harm comes to the patient, one can tie the intestine with a fine thread that is cut from an animal's intestine, in this manner: take the head of this intestinal thread which is very thin, and then tie at the head of this thread a fine twisted linen thread; then pass the thread through the needle, and sew the intestine, and bring it back to its place; and this way of suturing worms is nothing but according to the path of trust and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the small intestines, there is no trickery or remedy, except for subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	 of a fistula wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	 You should know that any wound or abscess, when it bursts open, is universally called a "fistula," and likewise when it is incised and discharges pus.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	 And a fistula is, according to the truth, a hard and white nodule that feels no pain, and it is also incised like the feather of a bird; sometimes it discharges clear pus, and other times thick; sometimes little, and other times enough; and I have spoken about this in the division of wounds, that any wound which does not heal, and there is no flesh on it, is only healed by one of the nine causes: that is to say, due to the smallness of the blood or body; or because of its evil nature; or because there is hard flesh within it, on the edges, which prevents the growth of flesh; or there is too much pus; or the place is rotten and the matter is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good for healing; or because the corruption is in the form of pestilence; or due to the nature of the region, digestion is slow, and healing is late, and it is swollen by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and their signs, and cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	 It is necessary that I inform you about the treatment of a fistula caused by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	 Know that fistulas occur in all parts of the body; for there are fistulas that come from large veins, and arteries, and nerves, or the liver, or the intestines, or the bladder, or some ribs, or the spine of the back, or some joints of the hands or feet; and so on, until it reaches the main part of the body, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	 And all the fistulas of this kind are difficult to heal, and there is only hard work and ignorance involved; and if there is a fistula that does not come up to the place I have mentioned, and you have confidence in the cure, and you can recognize it, take an iron or iron tent if the fistula is straight, seek it out; and if the fistula is crooked, look for it with a subtle tent of pine wood, because pine bends easily around the curvature; and if the fistula has many openings and you cannot well seek it out with tents, then irrigate it through one of the openings, because the moisture flows from one opening to another, and cleanses it; then seek it wisely as best you can, so that you may know whether there is bone or nerve inside, and cut it off deeply, and ask the patient carefully about the pain he feels at the touch of your hand, and where he feels it; and when you truly know where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein, or in any of the places I have told you about, cut according to what I have said, and remove the decayed flesh and rotten material inside; and then cure it until it is healed; and if the fistula is very deep in a straight place, then you must cut deeply as much as you can, then put moist tents soaked in vinegar at the top of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the excess that remains at the bottom; and then apply bandages with fresh meat until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this method, cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is rotten from the fistula, cut it out.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	 If a vein or nerve is cut in the main limbs, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, soak it until all the corruption is removed, then treat it with something that causes the flesh to heal until it is healed; and if it does not heal, and it returns as before, know that you have not reached the bottom: uncover and search until you reach the bottom, remove all the corruption, then restore the place; and if it is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	 If not, know that the corruption is too deep for you to reach; there is no other remedy but to leave it to nature; and if there is a small piece of bone corrupted, and you can pull it out with tweezers, then pull it out with an instrument suitable for this purpose, and if there are many bones, then pull them all out, leaving not one; and if moisture prevents you from doing so, and there is no error or fear, cut off the flesh, moisture, and skin, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	 And if you cannot remove them in an hour, then place on the wound something that causes rotting, and leave it until the flesh is rotten around the bones; and then the bones will be more easily removed; and if it is a large bone, such as from the leg or thigh, then wait only for the corruption to remove all the blackness, then restore the wound; and if there is a great part of putrefaction that reaches the marrow of the bone; then it must be cleaned and scraped all the way to the putrefaction, and then treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you may take an example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	 Il fut un jeune homme d'environ trente ans, qui eut une douleur dans sa jambe à cause de quelque chose qui est entré dans le corps, jusqu'à ce que les matières atteignent la jambe, et elle gonfla avec un grand abcès, et il n'y avait aucune raison pour l'ouvrir; mais les médecins par leur folie travaillèrent tellement qu'ils ouvrirent l'abcès, et beaucoup de matières en sortirent, et une fistule se forma, et il y eut beaucoup de trous qui laissaient échapper du pus et des humeurs du corps; et de nombreux médecins y cherchèrent un remède pendant deux ans, et il n'y avait personne compétent dans l'art de la guérison, jusqu'à ce que je sois appelé, et j'ai vu sa jambe et les médicaments avec lesquels on le traitait, et ce qui sortait par les trous en grande quantité; et la peau du jeune homme devenait rouge, et elle avait une teinte citron.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	 Je pitched a tent in one of these holes, and then searched all the holes, and found that one came up against another from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	 I hurried then, and cut into one of the holes until I exposed a part of the bone, which I found to be corrupted and perforated, and the corruption reached into the bone; I removed what appeared to me of the corrupted bone, thinking that there was no other corruption except what I removed; and began to treat the wound with healing medicines for a long time, but it did not heal; and then I redid it, and exposed the bone again as before, and found the corruption continued in the bone, which I removed, and then endeavored to heal the place; but I could not do so until I cut around a palm's width of the bone, and drew it out completely, then treated it with medicines; and it was quickly healed and sealed, and there was no need to restart the work except for the weakness of the patient, who could not endure it, and the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	 Car for the evacuation of blood, he often bled, but he was entirely healed, and in place of the bone, hard flesh grew, and it was of good disposition and caused no harm or opposite effect at all, neither going nor coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	 And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it must be treated in this manner: take a bandage and tie it to the end of the exposed bone, and command someone to stretch it upward; and put another thicker woolen bandage above the first bandage on the flesh above the bone, and extend the tip so that you draw the rotten flesh out from below, and uncover the flesh above the place where you wish to suture, so that the suture does not harm the flesh; and put a splint or a board underneath the bone to move and crush the rotten flesh; and it must be sutured as much as one can see and feel the corruption, and suture again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	 And if the bone is corrupted, and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, then uncover all the flesh; then put a coal underneath, and then use silk from one part to the other on the corruption, and let the silken thread be as long as the corruption is wide, as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut off the corrupted joint, and use the bone on the other side; and if the corruption is between two joints, there is no other way than to cut; and if the corruption is in the palm of the hand, or in the palm of the foot, this thing is very strong, but nonetheless you must seek out that corruption, how it opens; and cleanse it in all the ways that you can, but let the vein or nerve not be against you; and know that the instruments for cutting these bones are many, according to the position of the bones and their appearance, and their thickness and subtlety, and their size and smallness, and their hardness; and therefore it is necessary to prepare for each type of work its instrument; and know that the work will show you the instrument which you need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of diseases; so consider the instrument which you need according to what is needed.
dou feu	 of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	 The head rots either from within or without; and when you have treated that rotting with the cure of medicines, and they are not effective, then you must amputate that member up to the place where the rotting comes from, so that the patient escapes death, or the greater evil, which is the loss of the limb; and the sign is that the member turns black, as if it were burned by fire, and after the blackness, the rot spreads from one member to another, and affects the entire body; therefore hurry with amputation. And if it is due to the sting of some poisonous creatures, such as a sea scorpion or viper, if the rotting is at the tip of the finger, cut it off, and do not allow it to spread to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	 And if it reaches the hand, cut it at the joint, so that the corruption does not reach the arm; and if it reaches the arm, cut it with a knife; and if it passes the knife, then it is death, and no other treatment will avail except for the quantity of its strength; and do likewise when the corruption reaches the foot: if it reaches the first joint, cut it after the next joint; and if it reaches the foot, cut off the entire foot; and if it climbs up the leg, cut at the knee joint; and if it reaches above the knee, then there is no other device than to leave the patient to die; and the manner of cutting or sawing the limb is such that you bind it above and below, and extend a band downwards with one hand and another band upwards with the other hand, and cut away the flesh between the two bands by one fingerbreadth wide, so that the bone is exposed; then cut or saw, and place on each side a linen cloth, so that the saw does not touch the healthy part, and thus causes the patient further injury and abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	 And if blood flows when you work, then cauterize the place quickly, or put on some restricting powders; then return to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the wounded member with a suitable bandage, and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you that it happened to a man in his foot: there was a darkness that seemed like a burn from fire, and this corrosion first came on his big toe, so much so that it spread throughout the entire foot; and when the man saw the corrosion, he hastened to cover the foot, and it was healed; and a long time after, the corrosion returned to his big toe of the hand, and he came to me, and I put on repellent things after cleansing the body, and the corrosion could not be stopped; and he wanted me to cut off his hand, but I did not want to, for I hoped to repel the matter; and I also feared that if I cut off his hand, he might die, because the man's strength was weak; and he became completely desperate, and returned to his country, and hastened to cover his hand, and it was healed; and I have not told this story except so that others may learn from it, if they need to.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	 Some time an abscess comes in a fleshy place, and stays so long that it causes a great swelling of the flesh; then it roars and breaks open, and the flesh leaps out, and the place remains empty, just like a vessel; and the skin which is above is as delicate as fine cloth, and does not reach to the bone, nor to the nerve; and such an illness is called "sain," and is not called "fistula"; but if it is so elongated that it reaches to the bone in depth, then it is called "fistula"; and the skin is such that you can cut all around that skin, even when it is delicate, just like fine cloth; and it does not heal due to its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	 And if you believe that the skin is hardened, and the corruption is not deep, and the skin is thick with flesh, cure it with an enema like this: look if the breast is large, and the pus coming out of it is foul-smelling, then enema him with Egyptian medicine made like this: take as much resin, oil, and lead as you need, and put them to boil in a pot over fire until the medicine turns red and becomes as thick as honey; and then take some according to your needs, make it into water and honey, and enema the breast, and plug the opening; and leave the medicine inside for two hours, then remove it by squeezing out; do this many times, until the breast is cleaned, and the pus is removed; and sometimes enema with ash water, when this medicine is not present, and it is that you take ashes from a vine branch, and pour water over them, then strain it, and enema until you know that the breast is well cleaned; and if the patient cannot tolerate it, or the Egyptian medicine or the ash water, then enema with water and honey where there is a little crushed lead; or enema with honey and melted wine, as honey has the property of cleaning and washing, and wine makes the flesh dry out; and when you have done this, and you believe that the breast is well cleaned, then enema it with what produces flesh in it, and it is that you take finished plaster and make it with rose oil and wine; or enema with some medicines and onions, whose properties I have mentioned in the treatment of onions; and if the opening of the breast is small, and the tube of the enema cannot enter, then widen it a little with an iron, and put in a piece of Egyptian ointment, or basilicon ointment, until it is widened; and if the wound is too wide, then stitch it up and leave only one place where the enema can enter, and if the opening that discharges pus is higher, then cut it lower than the current location.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	 When the abscess is ripe, do not allow flesh to be cut out; and if you cannot cut open the breast as you wish, prepare it in such a way that the abscess runs to the lowest place there is, for when the abscess is ripe, no flesh should be cut out. And if you cannot cut open the breast as you wish, prepare it in this manner: let the abscess run lightly downwards and leave nothing of the abscess; and take consolidative medicines to put on the wound, and extend over a cloth of linen that covers all the wound; then cut with force towards the opening of the breast, making the hole wider than the first, then spread soft ointment over another cloth according to the size of the opening, and place it over the opening of the wound to lighten the abscess, and do not remove the large cloth until after many days, but once; and that which is on the opening of the breast, often remove it to remove the abscess, and know what comes out of the abscess, whether it is venom or pus or enough, or digested, or undigested; and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not. And when your medicine has been spread in this way and you see the nature that leaps up to the opening of the wound, know that the breast has already healed, and health approaches; and then uncover it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you uncover the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	 And if the breast throws up undigested food after many days, know that the breast does not heal.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	 And if subtle poisons have passed after a long time, do not despair of health, for health approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	 And there are men in whom the flesh of their wounds is delayed in healing, and others who do the opposite; and if undigested food comes up from the breast after many days, know that the breast does not heal; and if the breast delays in healing and is distant, then apply dry and moist substances and dry in virtue, as diaphoretic ointment, for it contains a great deal of vitriol, and this is the last medicine; take diaphoretic ointment, and make it with rose oil, and sprinkle it with old wine equal in substance; then cook it and use it; and the same done cooked thickens better when diaphoretic ointment is not present, or you take myrrh and aloe and incense, and grind them, and powder over honey when it is on the fire; and then glue a cloth, and apply it to the breast; and sometimes they administer long-acting astringent, and celestial lily roots, which are like chickpea flour and cinnamon; and use either simple or compound: grind them, and make a powder, and put on the honey I mentioned, and use it; and if the cure is prolonged, and not cured by this cure, then know that the corruption is deep, and affects the bone, or hard members, or ligaments; then treat the treatment of fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	 of the fingertip abscess
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	 A panarice is an abscess that forms under the fingertip or toe, or sometimes in other places; and when it becomes inflamed, if one does not take care of it, then there comes an ugly abscess, and it runs and throws pus until it reaches the root of the nail, and perhaps it will reach all the way; and gangrene sets in up to the bone, causing a foul pain, and the tip of the finger becomes swollen, and its color turns red.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	 When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, then you must cut off with an iron knife all the remaining excess of the nail, then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The cautery is a great help if the bone is healthy, and the nail is intact; and if the nail presses into the flesh, and begins to pierce, and wounds it, then you must place the razor under the nail that touches the flesh, and push it up, and cut off that delicate flesh lightly and subtly, and apply burning and corrosive medicines on top of the remaining flesh to remove everything; then treat with onions until it heals.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	 And if the corruption is in the bone, cut it away and draw strongly, for as long as the corrupt bone remains, it cannot heal; and if you see the finger become corrupt, cut it off at one of our joints as previously mentioned, then treat until it heals; and if it is struck and swollen, causing great pain, it is necessary that you first drain it; then cut the nail diagonally from above with a sharp spatula, taking care not to let the cut reach the flesh beneath the nail, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if it does happen, apply something soothing on top.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	 The pain of the shoulder of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	 The two thumbs that are born in the hands of some men by chance are all fleshly, and sometimes there is one with bones, and sometimes there is a nail, and sometimes they grow from the root of the joint, or their birthplace is in some of our fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	 That which is born in the tip of the thumb does not move, and that which is born at the joint of the thumb sometimes moves; the size of the one which is fleshy is light, in this manner: cut it away at its root with a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	 That which grows from the root of the joint is difficult to cure; then use a knife.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 In the case of one who is born or should at the anus, it is necessary that you first cut the flesh roundly down to the bone, then cut the bone with a suitable saw, then heal it until it is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	 The swelling that comes to the two together comes from birth, or from the joining of a wound, or from burning by fire, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	 You must cut that swelling so that the limbs may repair according to their natural forms; then place between two tents or cloths moistened with rose oil, so that they do not join; or you put between two thin sheets of lead until the place is healed as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	 If suddenly one of his fingers comes with the palm, cut that joint as needed.
des vils	 of the fingers
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	 The veins are large and swollen with an excess of black bile that comes in many parts of the body; and it happens more in the legs of those who walk and work and carry than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	 Therefore, you should administer purging of bile to him, and then treat him with a plaster.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	 The treatment of iron is in two ways: one is that you cut the veins and draw out the black blood; and the other way is that you raise the vein and drain it completely.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	 The incision is done in this manner: first, bathe the patient's leg in very hot water until the large vein is made thin; then press on the patient's leg from above the hip to below the knee; then cut the vein in one place, or two, or three, with a wide incision; then lift and draw out the black blood into your hand, from one end to the other, as much blood as the patient's constitution can bear; and then bind it, and instruct him to eat foods that increase black bile; and repeat the evacuation and treatment when the veins are full, and benefit the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The lifting of it is done in this manner: lift the leg of the patient, if there is a lot of hair, then put it in a bath, and wash the leg with hot water until it turns red, and swell the veins; and if you have no bath, heat it by the fire, and then cut towards the vein from the knee to the ankle or in the lower part below the ankle; then strip the skin with scissors, and peel the vein from each side, until it is visible when touched; and one sees it red and black, and when it enters the skin it seems like a white cord; then push the reed below, until it is lifted from the skin, then lightly peel another skin, then cut in another place above three fingers; then strip the skin above the vein until it is visible, then lift with the reed as you have done, and peel another skin as you did first; then cut another incision, or several if you need them, then lift and cut at the toe of the foot, then pull and lift up to the second incision; then draw from one incision to another, until it comes out completely, then cut; and if you cannot draw and lift it, put a needle with a strong double thread, and pull and draw it, and put a reed below, and turn your hand from side to side, until it comes out; and be careful that it does not cut, because if it cuts, it cannot be drawn or lifted, and this causes harm to the patient; and when you have completely drawn it, place wet wool in wine and rose oil on the place of the wound; and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	 And if the face is constricted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must split it crookedly, but do not cut it off; and treat it as we have previously said.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	 The shape of the iron used to cut the face is curved, and does not cut, so that it cuts the vein; and it is thickly curved, for if it were thin, it would cut the vein. Let it be thick as we have said, and here is the shape:
de la voinne civile	 of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	 This vein is injected into the legs, in hot places where no grass or trees grow, and in dry earth; and perhaps it grows elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens because of the corruption that comes from under the skin, as it does within the body with serpents and worms, injected between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	 And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are such that it comes into the leg a very great inflammation, then the place changes, and the vein begins to emerge, just like the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	 And when the head appears, it is necessary that you wrap around it a piece of linen from three and a half to two and a half [widths], and also the knot, and let the linen hang at the leg, and each time some comes out due to lack, wrap it again with the linen and the knot; and if it is too long, cut off part of it, and wrap the rest, and do not cut it near its root until all has come out; for if you cut it, it will enter into the flesh, and cause an abscess and putrefaction in the place, and a bad disease; therefore, for this reason, it is necessary that it be treated bit by bit until the end, and nothing remains in the body; and sometimes this vein, when it is treated from five palms long, or ten, and one man came to me whose [vein] issued ten palms long, and when you cut it, it will expel a stream or pus, and pierce it until it all comes out; and empty the matter that is inside, and apply medicines that prevent putrefaction every day, then treat it as [you would] with abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	 And sometimes at this vein there are less pains, and especially when it opens in the joint of the foot, or in the foot, and then there is much peril, and from which blood flows out; heal it then as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	 worms that grow between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	 This disease is called in our land "cattle disease," because it often affects cattle, and it is a small worm that grows between skin and flesh, and goes through the whole body rising and falling, and one feels it well when moving from member to member, until it bursts the skin where it goes, and spills out; and it is infested by the corruption of some humors, as come worms and snakes and loaches and roundworms in the belly; and one fears its malice, for when it goes through the body, and it rises to the head, and it comes to the eye, perhaps enters, and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	 When you see it being treated and pulled out, one cannot do so except when it goes away: therefore, you must tie the place above and below with a strong ligature very tightly, then cut above and pull strongly; and if the pus is deep in the flesh, and you do not find it, cauterize it with fire on top until it dies; and the greatest harm that it does is that it causes the eye to run, as we have said; and if you see it coming towards the head near the eye, firmly hold under it the sorcil, then cut above, and pull strongly; and one must use the patient for cleansing of the body with dissolving medicines for evil humors, and avoid foods that cause putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	 Of the pain that comes from flatulence
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	 This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes to certain members, and then moves from member to member; and I have seen what I tell you.
