Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	 And if you doubt that the bone will move, use bands, and place a wider and stronger band over the fracture than the others, and let there be two finger widths between each band, and let each band be so large that it extends three finger widths beyond the fracture on each side; then pull up on the bands, as I said at the beginning of the chapter on the fracture, more strongly and less widely.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	 And if you see the base of the bands and their tightening, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the broken member, and you doubt that the abscess is hot, leave it to bind until the seventh day, as we have said; then look at the binding every three days, lest itching or swelling come to the place, or the nourishment cannot reach the member because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	 If you receive it, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	 And if no such accidents occur, do not unbind it until after three days or more, and the patient sleeps on his back, and has his hands on his stomach; and place a cushion full of wool equally under the shoulder, and observe every hour of the day or night that the appearance of the broken limb does not move, or that the bandage is not softened; then receive it by the power of medicine, and give him the food that we have mentioned before, in such a way that the food is first subtle; and when he begins to recover, let it be thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	 And it is customary that the shoulder and the leg should be kept bound for forty days in total; and then one should unbind it and administer baths and medications of onions to heal the place.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	 And if the constriction is ugly and clogged, it will take days or two months to loosen.
de la brisure du bras	 of the arm's fracture
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	 The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "two ulnae," one of which is small, and this is the one that follows the forearm; and the other is large, and it is this one that is beneath, towards the little finger; perhaps only the large ulna breaks, or the small one, and perhaps both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	 When the small ulna is broken, the restoration is light and the healing; but when the large one is broken, then the healing is bad, and more serious than when both are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	 If it is the small bone that is broken alone, then you should extend it slightly and set it straight.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	 And if it is the large bone, then you must pull harder; and stretch it on a pillow, and grasp the little finger of the hand higher than the others, and the small toe lower than the others, and let the patient be crossed over himself, and the pillow in front of him higher, so that the patient does not suffer any labor; then let the ministers extend their arms towards the part under his hand or on the ligament, and another minister to the other above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	 Then let the physician set it straight, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	 And if the fracture is in pieces, then put each one in its place; and if there is any that sticks out which you cannot restore to its place, then cut it off and remove it, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	 And if with the break is a wound, I have spoken of it in a specific chapter; so take the treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	 And if in the beginning of the treatment such abscesses appear, then glue a cloth made of rose oil and white wax, so that it is not too hard nor too soft; and tie the cloth on top delicately, until those abscesses are calmed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	 And then remove the wax, and apply the poultice of mill powder with plenty of egg, then place the splints, and let the splint on the break be always a little stronger and a bit wider than the others; and know that there should be six splints on the arm in various positions: whether the break is in one of the bones or two; and press more on the break than elsewhere, and always less by lengthening, as I said at the beginning of the chapter; and let the cloths that are on the break be soft and moist, and not hard nor rough; and let the thread used for binding be made of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	 And return the limb and the ligament after some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	 And if some evil accident happens to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, you should rinse the limb with hot water until the itch is relieved; and do not let the limb rest too tightly.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	 And then begin the splinting again, and if the ligament is softened and the bone dislocated, or similar things, set it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	 And if you take care that the nourishment cannot reach the limb because it is too narrow, then you should soften it in a poultice and leave it like this for some days until the nourishment reaches there, and then splint it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	 Et si aucune de ces choses que nous avons dites ne vient au malade, alors ne le délier pas avant vingt jours.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	 Et si aucune de ces choses que nous avons dites ne vient au malade, alors ne le délier pas avant vingt jours. Si, ou dans lequel cas, on peut lier les mains du patient autour de son cou, et que ses bras soient égaux, et qu'il prenne garde aux mouvements et aux secousses, et qu'il dorme sur le dos; et sachez que cette fracture est guérie en trente jours ou trente-cinq, et peut-être même en vingt jours, selon les compositions et les complexions des vertus.
de la brisure de la main	 De la fracture de la main
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	 Sachez que dans le dos de la main et aux jointures des doigts il arrive peu de fractures, et qu'il ne s'y produit que des entorses à plusieurs reprises.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	 And when the sole of the hand is broken or bent, it is necessary that the patient sit cross-legged, and sit straight in front of him equally; then he places his hand on the extended table, and the attendant extends the broken bones, and sets them equal with pliers, until they are well joined; and applies the dressing and bandages, if pus forms, then place a splint according to the size of the place; and let it be wrapped in a linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	 And if the break is around the base of the palm, make a sphere of cloths, and instruct the patient to tie it to his broken palm; and then bind it with a long cloth, and let the splint be as soft as the palm of the hand, and bind it, as needed.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	 And if the fracture is at the tip, it is necessary that you place a splint on top and another below at the palm, so that the hand is open and straight, then tie all around the hand, and secure the bandage between the two fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	 And if the break occurs at any of the fingers, if it is dislocated, straighten it as needed; and bind it with the palm, and if you see fit place a small straight splint to lift the fracture, so that it does not move; and if the fracture is in the other finger, such as the index or one of the others, straighten it, and bind it with the adjacent healthy finger; either tie them all together, whichever works better, or place a splint on top, like in the thumb; and be cautious in restoration and abscess management, and assist those who come, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	 of a broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	 The bone of the thigh is often broken, and it can be seen when it turns to the front and back; and the restoration is such that one tie is placed above the break, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	 And the patient lies on his back, then each assistant extends their tie equally to their side; and this is when the break is in the middle of the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	 And if the break is near the root of the thigh, then one of the ties should be towards the knee, and the other tie below the break.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	 And likewise if it is near the knee, then the tie should be at the knee and the extension downwards; then let the physician set the bone equal with his two hands until it is according to its natural shape, and then apply the plaster and bandage, unless pustules come out.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	 And if there is a hot abscess, let it calm down before you return to your work and treatment; the procedure is done in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	 And it is necessary that you wrap on the break a bandage of strong linen in two or three layers, leaving the ends protruding; then turn the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the nail, and insert a long thread between the thigh and the leg, next to the knee below, and the ends of the thread come up top; then wrap the bandage around the leg and the thigh, then place splints on the break, and put a splint on the bone of the leg; then fill the space between the leg and the thigh with soft cloths to distribute the pressure evenly, then begin to tie strongly three or four times on the break; and as you go higher on the break, reduce the tightness; then catch the two ends of the thread that you inserted between the leg and the thigh, and secure three splints that are on top, then return below to the end of the thread, so that you come next to the foot; and secure it, so that it does not move from its place, then leave it thus, since there will be neither abscess nor swelling nor anything similar.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	 And if it happens, then dislocate it, and direct it as it comes, as we have said many times; and if there are bone fragments that prick, then they must be removed, if possible; and if not possible, then the place must be split open, and pull hard; and heal it as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	 And sometimes the thigh is broken as if one puts splints in it, as in the shoulder and the arm; however, in such a restoration, the patient does not linger.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	 And know that the thigh is restored in 40 days, or a little less or more, depending on the diversity of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	 of the tendon of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	 Know that in the tendon of the knee there is little fracture, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	 And if it breaks, it is only a fissure or a hole, and this happens in every wound, both in open and closed wounds, and everyone feels it well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And the restoration is such that you should join together what is round at its ends as much as possible; then apply the plaster, and place a round bandage on it, if needed, and fasten it as necessary, then follow all the precautions that we have mentioned in other fractures, such as abscess or similar; for each incident, use what is appropriate until he is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	 Of the breaking of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	 Know that in the leg there are two bones; one is rightly called «mustelz», and the other is called «foscile»; and all kinds of breaks happen as they do in the arm, and therefore the restoration is the same as for the arm, and the work is completely the same. And if both bones are broken together, then the leg turns in all directions.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	 And if the smaller bone is broken, it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	 And if the larger bone is broken, one feels great pain, and it can be seen well; and it turns downward.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	 Then apply traction, and align it well, and tie the splints evenly; but nevertheless, if the break is ugly, and there are many pieces, then the traction should be less and lighter; and adjust according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when you have completed your work, take two strips of wood shavings that wrap around the leg on one side and the other, and they should be as long as the leg from the knee downwards; then wrap it in two places with a bandage above and below, and tie it in the middle likewise, and at this time the leg will not be able to bend to the right or to the left, and thus it is good; and some add two splints the length of the leg, and they are made of wood, and one places the leg there to prevent movement, and one properly does this in a fracture where there is a wound; and move each day the leg, to see if there is an abscess or other accident; and cure it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	 Of the fracture of the foot bones
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	 At the ankle, there is no fracture, but sometimes the foot bones break and the two bones, and in this case, it happens more often as a shattering in various ways.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	 And if the foot bones break and you see these bones overriding each other, put the patient's foot on the ground as if he wanted to walk, then place your foot on top of his where the bones are raised, then press until they return to their place; then apply a poultice and wool above, and place under the sole of the foot a small board with two plain keys, then bind the foot tightly, after which you wrap bandages around it and other things that you need.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	 And when three days or four have passed, then dislocate the ligament, for you will find the bones equal, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	 And if any of the two are broken, restore them as we have said for the fingers of the hand; then place on the broken finger a splint according to the length of the finger, and it should be a little wider, then place under the foot the board that I mentioned, and bind it tightly; and if there are two or three, or more, broken, then place on each finger a splint according to its size, wrapped in a piece of linen, and bind the board under the foot; and let it stand on the top of the board outside the stomach of the foot, so that it holds well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	 And it is necessary that you do not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, as we have said; and treat each case as appropriate.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	 of the bone of the wrist
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 When the bone of the woman's birth canal is broken, have her sit spread-legged, then lean her back towards the rear, and hold her in that position; then fill the gap of the woman's birth canal with cotton, and put in as much as I can fit; then raise the woman up, and lift her bottom a little at a time, until the cotton jumps out to the entrance of the birth canal, and the bone returns with the cotton; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has finished urinating, replace it, and do this for 7 days or so: thus the fracture will be healed, and if you wish, take a sheep's bladder, and attach a reed to the opening, and blow up the entire bladder inside the birth canal; then inflate the reed very strongly, until the bladder is fully inflated inside: thus the fracture of the birth canal will return; then fill it with cotton, and leave it that way for some days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	 Et when the bones of the hand are broken, whether in man or woman, restore them as we have said for the hip bone; and these breaks are not hidden from those who apply their study and practice to it, and understand my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	 For breakings signify in many arrangements the right way of restoration; understand this then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	 In the penis, when it is broken, take a goose neck and put the penis in it; then wrap cloths around it, and let it stay for three days, and he will be quickly cured.
de brisure avec plaie	 of breaking with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	 It is necessary for someone who has a breaking with wound, especially if it is large, such as the bone of the thigh or shoulder or similar, that he be cauterized immediately, so that the cauteries that we have mentioned prove it.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	 And if the wound heals, then seal it with vitriol, if you have nothing else; then begin again to restore the break in that same hour, or that day, if no abscess forms there.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	 And if an abscess forms there, then leave the restoration until the ninth day, until the abscess is calmed; and do not touch it on the third or fourth day, for you will cause evil to come.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	 And if the broken bone is protruding from the surface of the skin, then you must handle it lightly with your hands, with slight extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	 And if the extension is not ready to be handled equally with your hands, then reset it with this iron instrument which has seven or eight inches in length, and its width should match the size of the wound; and for this reason, the physician needs three or four [of these instruments], according to what he needs for each fracture treatment; and let it be round and slightly thick, so that it does not bend under pressure on the limb during your work, and let it be sharp at the tip, and thick from the middle forward, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	 And it is called "palainche", for which reason the curved head should be placed on the top of the exposed bone; and press down once, until it returns, and let them be equal to each other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	 And if the fracture is subtle, and the instrument cannot well take the bone, then it is necessary that you cut off the head of the bone, so that the instrument has power over it.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	 And if you cannot return the bone, as we have said, then strike it with an appropriate instrument, either a knife or a saw, to your ability; then raise that which remains in the bone by roughness and small splinters.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	 And when the bone is returned, and the patient feels great pain afterward, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	 If it is so that the joint remains in place, then moisten a cloth in black stiptic wine, and properly if it is in summer; and do not put any ointment or other thing on the wound where there is oil, lest it bring about putrefaction and corruption; then administer steel pins after you have reset the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cut the bandage all around, according to the size of the wound, and be well aware that the wound is not constricted with the fracture; and many times have foolish physicians done this, and brought about death or corrosion in the patient sometimes; and let the constriction be softer and gentler than other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	 And if the wound is bad or large, and you fear that an evil accident may happen, as we have said, and you find pain in the place, then it is not fitting to put on bandages; but wrap around it, instead of bandages, hard cloths, and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	 And when you see after one day or two that the swelling begins to grow on the wound, then remove everything you have put on in all haste, and apply healing ointment for wounds, such as tetracycline ointment and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	 And it is necessary that you unbind the limb twice a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it is healed and cured.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	 And it is necessary that the limb be prepared in such a way that the bone descends lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	 And if many days pass and it cannot be joined together but the bone returns again, know that there are small pieces of bone, for which you must explore the wound with a probe, and remove all these loose pieces that cause this pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	 And if an ulcer comes to the place, or another manner of corruption, it is necessary that you cure it, according to what he says in this chapter before.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	 And when the bone is broken and exposed on the limb, as the thigh or shoulder bones, and other similar large members, do not pull it out, for many times death follows, but leave it until it rots; perhaps it will fall off by itself after twenty or thirty days, then cure the wound if you can; and if you cannot, then leave it. xspace: When the bone is exposed, don't remove it, let it rot and fall off on its own. After 20-30 days, treat the wound if possible.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	 over bruises that come onto the sore
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	 We often see them after the healing of the bruising, especially when it is near the joint, and the appearance of the limb is unsightly; and by chance the member cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	 So beware if the nose is fresh: then administer styptic medicines, such as aloes, frankincense, and myrrh, and sarcocolla, cassia, and similar others; whichever of these you take, or all together, and make a poultice with styptic wine or plenty of egg or oil; and put it on the swelling in wool, and bind it well, and do not unbind for many days; and then unbind, and start another one, until the swelling is gone; or you bind on a well-made piece of lead; for the property of lead is such that it removes all the swellings from the members; and if the swelling has already hardened like stone, and it needs to be removed, then shave off the top, and make the excess apparent; or have it scraped by some scraper, until it is removed, and treat until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	 of the limb which is weak after the healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	 When the bone fracture is healed, and afterward the limb remains weak and thin, this happens for many reasons: one of which is because it was bandaged too tightly and not bandaged as it should have been; or because there were too many bandages, preventing nourishment from reaching the limb; or due to excessive bleeding; or because of too much movement, not at the right time; or because the person has little blood in their body, causing weakness.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	 And the treatment is such that you should make the patient eat, and keep their body soft, until the blood increases in them; and administer baths, and give them joy and cheer; then apply wax to the limb, so that the wax attracts abundant nourishment, and frequently wash it with warm water, so that the nourishment flows to the limb; and let it return to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	 About the twisted limb after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	 When the limb is twisted after restoration, and broken bones are visible, and the shape of the limb is ugly, nevertheless it does not lose its natural function: do not believe the fools who say that one must break the limb again; many foolish doctors have done this in our land; and these actions are blamed, and great evils come from them, and possibly death. However, if the nodules and tortures are fresh, they must be treated with hot water or softening herbs, such as leaves of vismalva, roots, mellilotus, and similar things; and make a softening plaster, such as well-made diquilon, and take the juice of vismalva, and mix it with goose fat or sesame oil, and make a plaster on top; or take fat figs, and crush them with linseed flour, and similar medicines that weaken the hardening.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	 And sometimes the dislocation is removed by continuously and vigorously rubbing with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	 And let there be gentle movement applied to the member each hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	 And if the curvature is hardened like stone and needs to be removed with an iron, it must be cut down to the bone with a sharp, light incision; and put skill and effort into the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	 Here begins the book on dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	 Dislocation is the displacement of a joint from its proper place, so that it cannot move, and the limb is misshapen, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	 When dislocation occurs in someone, they must be brought back to sense immediately. ‌
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	 Because if one waits, the place swells, and perhaps it is barely set back in place; therefore, it should not be moved while it is swollen: many times it brings spasms and other pains; however, when this happens, make the patient fast, then leave him until the abscess subsides; then soak the member in hot water and oil, then reset it gently, and cure each member as it comes into its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	 And I have arranged the chapters of the dislocations from the head down to the feet.
des mandibules	 of the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	 It rarely happens that the jaws are dislocated together, and the dislocation of both is according to two manners: either they are a little removed from their place and slightly softened; or they are completely dislocated and hang down towards the chest, and saliva runs out of the mouth which he cannot hold, nor can he close his mouth, and his tongue is wrapped with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	 When the dislocation is small, it returns by itself in many ways.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	 And if it is entire and complete, then you must reset it quickly, and do not delay; and in such a manner that the assistant holds the patient's head, and the doctor places his finger from one of his hands at the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, if the dislocation is of two parts; and the other two hands should be free, to balance; and instruct the patient to soften his jaws, and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	 And the doctor should set it equally, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	 And if the return is difficult, even if it is the two jaws together, then wash them with hot water and oil, until you reset them lightly; do not delay in resetting, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	 And when they are brought back into alignment, and the patient's mouth is closed without softening, place damp cloths on a plaster made of rose oil and wax, then bind it lightly with soft bands; and let the patient sleep on their back, with their head between two pillows, so that it does not move to the right or left, nor does it try to open its mouth, but take light food until the pain is relieved and the jaws are closed; and then chew what one wants lightly, and do not strain to open the mouth for eating and drinking, until the jaw is well bound and healed.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	 And if the two jaws cannot be set right within an hour and are not restored to their proper places, fever and abscesses follow, and perhaps a ruptured bowel, and possibly vomiting of clear bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	 And when you see this, then know that it is a disaster; and many times he who experiences it dies within nine days.
de la forcelle	 from the armpit
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	 The armpit cannot dislocate from the inside of the body or from the hip, and sometimes it is dislocated by force, and one feels it well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	 And the restoration is such that the patient often lies on his back and extends his arms; and then presses the place strongly with your palm, and it will return; then apply a poultice and bandage, and tighten it; and the head which is towards the side cannot dislocate; if not, and if it dislocates sometimes, reset it to its place as we have said; then apply a poultice and bandage, and tighten it, and instruct the patient to rest until he is healed; and thus likewise the shoulder joint is restored when it is displaced from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	 of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	 Know that the shoulder is dislocated only in three ways: one way is that it dislocates at the underside of the socket; and the second is at the side of the ribs; and sometimes it dislocates at the top, which happens rarely; and it does not dislocate behind the shoulder, nor inside due to the nerves; and often it dislocates downwards towards the socket, especially in those who have little flesh, for in them it jumps quickly; in those who have enough flesh, it jumps with difficulty, and returns with difficulty.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	 And sometimes it happens to some men due to injury or breakage, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they think that it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	 It is therefore necessary that you test it, until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	 And the dislocation is known when it descends towards the shoulder blade, and there is a difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find a manifest diversity between them; and you will find at the head of the shoulder a depression, and under the shoulder blade the head of the shoulder, as if it were an egg; and the patient cannot bring his hand to his nose, nor move in any way; and likewise, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, for you will find it manifestly under the shoulder blade; and this manner of dislocation is not easy to return when it is new, or if the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	 And the manner is that the servant lifts the hand of the patient high, then places his fingers under the elbow, and lifts the joint forcefully high into its place; and the servant lifts the hand, extends it high, then places it underneath; thus it will come quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	 And if it does not come as we have said within a few days after, then the patient must be bathed in hot water; and let there be administered to him a softening and soothing ointment, such as a decoction of althaea, fenugreek, and melilot in water, and it should be applied; then let the patient be laid on his back, and place under the elbow a pad of cloth equal in thickness, neither too soft nor too hard; then let the physician place his heel on the pad, and lift the shoulder blade gently, and pull the hand of the patient; and another servant should hold the head of the patient so that it does not move downward; that shoulder returns immediately, and if you see it thus, reset it according to this manner: and it is that you make present a man who is larger than the patient; and let him stand straight beside the side, and press his shoulder under the elbow of the patient, and lift the elbow high so that the patient hangs in the air; and another servant should pull the hand of the patient down toward the stomach.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	 And if the patient is too weak, then some heavy object should be placed with him, and the dislocation will return now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	 And it can also be reset in another way: and it is that one drives a long log into the ground, so that the head is as round as a fist, neither too thick nor too thin; then let it be placed under the patient, but he should have soft cushions on top, and the patient should stand alongside the log; then let his hand be extended downwards on the other side in this manner, and the joint will quickly return to its place; and if it does not wish to return for all these things that we have said, then perform this treatment: take a log two arms long and four thumbs wide, which has a head rounded so as to enter deeply under the armpit, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	 Then lift the patient onto the top of the pole under the cloth, so that the pole does not hurt the patient. Then place it underneath the patient's seat; and stretch one arm along the pole, and bind the shoulder to the pole, and the arm at the wrist. Then place the arm on a wide step of a ladder, and let the hand hang down, and let the body hang from the other side: the joint will then be reduced.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	 And when it is in place, whichever way it may be, you must put underneath the seat an equal sphere of wool, then apply the plaster prepared with mill powder, with incense and egg white, over the entire shoulder and around it. Then fasten it securely under the seat, and turn the ligature over the plaster, and encircle the hand around its neck, and let the hand remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	 And it is necessary that he eats little, so that the limb may be comfortable, for it will heal faster; and then eat more after 5 or 7 days, and move it; and if it is stiffened and not softened, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	 And if the juncture is out of place due to moisture that has come there, or for another reason, it is necessary that you apply cauteries to three places, as is described in the chapter on cauteries.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	 And if you do all this, and it dislocates again after seven days, and the juncture does not stay in place, and cannot lift its arm up, then know that the nerves at the top of the shoulder are cut or stretched or softened; and know that the juncture will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 The dislocation that is towards the foot and the breastbone, or the back, is caused by pushing and stretching of the hands, and another measure is administered there; and care until it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	 And if after the healing comes stiffness in the limb, and slowness in movement, then let the patient take many baths until that stiffness is relieved, and it returns to its original condition.
de la dislocation dou coute	 of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	 Know that the shoulder joint is easily dislocated and just as easily returns; and if it has dislocated from all sides, especially in front and behind, and the dislocation is not repaid, because one can see it well and feel it well; and it dislocates according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	 And when you join the sick member with the healthy one, then you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	 Because the joint is dislocated, and he cannot bend his arm, nor can he touch his shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	 And it is necessary that you reset it before any abscesses form there, because if abscesses were to form, then it would be difficult to reset; and perhaps it cannot be completely reset, especially when it is in the back; this is worse than other dislocations, and causes greater pain, and perhaps death will follow.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	 And the resetting is thus: when it can be reset, that you extend his hand with both of your hands; and let his arm be spread out, and the hands of the healer around the joint, above and below, and push the joint back together at its base, or at the root of his palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	 And if the dislocation is forward, then it returns when he folds his hand to his hand, and strikes the root of the palm with the knife that is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	 And if it does not want to return to its place, then administer strong extension; and it is that two ministers extend the arm, and hold it with two hands, so that it does not move at the extension; then turn the arm from each side, after you have wrapped a long and wide double cloth around it; and when the patient joins the joint to his hand, then anoint it with some oil to soften the joint, then push the joint strongly, until it returns; and when it is in place, then put on a dry plaster with some egg, and hold it strongly, and bind the arm to the patient's neck, and leave it for some days, then unbind.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	 And if the joint is firmly in its place, then unbind the ligament and leave it; and if you see that the joint does not bind well, then begin again with the poultice and the ligament, and leave it thus for some days, until it is firmly set; then unbind.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	 And if he feels pain after the setting of the joint, and it moves, then wash and rub it well, and press until it is eased; or you put on the joint a greasy piece of sheep fat, then leave it one day and one night, then remove it, and make him enter the bath; and when he sweats, if you rub the joint gently, then put the fat back on, and then enter the bath; and do this two or three times, until it is healed; and if you see, put on a moist heated cow's dung with butter, and bind it up; so it will return to its place.
li dislocation de la main	 The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	 The joint of the hand is dislocated, and its return is slight, more than other joints. However, it must be returned to its place quickly, in the very hour that it is dislocated, before the place swells or becomes hot with abscess.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	 And the resetting is done by placing the sick hand on a table, and the assistant extends his hand, and the doctor places it evenly, so that he places his palm over the appearance of the joint, and pushes until it returns. However, you must check if it is well in place; then the patient places the back of his hand on the table for the extension and resetting.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	 And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, then let the patient place the back of their hand on a table, and let the physician place his hand on that appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	 If it returns now, it is good; if not, then restrain with soothing plasters for abscesses such as these, and leave it thus without recurring.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	 And if he cannot tolerate it and you cannot put it back in place after some days, then the joint remains crooked; and it does no harm to the patient except that as long as his hand is wet, he cannot grasp anything: then know that the nerves or blood vessels are cut; there is no other remedy except to cauterize near the wound, and perhaps nothing else will help. ›
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	 And when the hand is in place, put on the poultice that we have mentioned, then bind it and leave it for 5 days, then unbind and let it be thus.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if he cannot move it well, and there is some stiffness, then moisten it with hot water and rub until it is healthy.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	 Of the dislocation of the fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	 Sometimes the fingers of the hand are dislocated at each part, sometimes at the back of the palm or the front; then straighten the finger and push the dislocation towards your thumb until it returns, then support the head of the finger and bend it towards the part where it is dislocated; and leave it for 2 days, and then make it equal that day; and bind the nut as we have said, and unbind after a day, and make it move, and rebind the nut; and do this often, until it is tight, and do the same if it is dislocated at the front of the hand, and do as you did before until it is healthy; and do the same when it is dislocated on another part.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	 of the dislocation of the spine of the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	 When the spine of the back or neck is dislocated, and there are several dislocations, there is no cure, for death hastens the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	 And the signs are that he throws out feces without his will, and cannot hold it back, and often some members are paralyzed, either both thighs or both arms or one, and often the spine moves in four parts; the one that moves to the rear is called "gilbositez": the cure for this is that you restore if the gilbositez comes from childhood: there is no cure or healing for all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	 And the one that comes from falling or from blows or similar things, the ancients spoke of cures with great words, in which there is not always great benefit; but I have shortened it according to my intention, and have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	 I say that in the swelling that comes to the chest in front, there is neither wisdom nor health; and similarly for that which comes directly on two sides, and one cannot cure except for that which comes specifically to the back, as I say. And it must be that the patient lies flat on his face in a level place, and has support beneath him so he does not get injured. Then stick a brand into the ground at the head firmly, and another at the feet; tie a rope around the ankles of the patient, and another at the knees, and the ankles; and two assistants should know the ropes, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two brands. And let them be well tightened, the brands as we have said, and the master places his palms on the spine firmly until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	 And if it does not return with this treatment, then take a board of three arms in length, and place it underneath the patient, and let the patient be on the side, and push the head of the board underneath the patient, then place the middle of the board on the spine; and let the doctor place his feet on the other end of the board, and press well, until it returns to its place; and if you see fit, do this also for the shoulder that turns towards the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	 And it is that you place two stakes at the head of the patient one arm's length apart, and towards the feet two others, and there should be between each stake a palm's length in height; and each stake should have a hole through which the shoulder passes, and let the stakes be firmly planted in the ground so that they do not move; and between each pair of stakes there should be another turning stake on which the ropes turn, and between the two turning stakes there should be two small stakes one palm's length long to turn the shoulder; and then tie the rope that is among the poles to the shoulder towards the head, and the other rope to the other shoulder towards the feet, and each of the assistants turns his stake all along the rope, and the master straightens the spine as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	 And when it is equalized, apply a desiccating plaster with plenty of egg, then the gauze, then a bandage three fingers long, which soaks up the place of yellowness and the healthy part of the vertebra, then bind with a ligature, as we have said, and let the patient use subtle nursing until he is cured; and if anything happens at the end of the cure, it is necessary to administer softening and soothing medicines with the bandage that we mentioned earlier; sometimes one gives a piece of lead, and sometimes it appears in the lower vertebra of the back, and one thinks this is dislocation; but it is the bone that opens, for which one must not have presumption: perhaps it would bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	 Dislocation of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	 Know that in the hip and shoulder joints, dislocation occurs alone, and it does not happen as in other joints; and the hip joint is dislocated according to four parts: inside and outside, front and back; and it is more inside one place than another, and hardly ever dislocates in front or back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	 The sign of its inside dislocation is that when the leg of the sick person is joined with the healthy one, it is longer, and the knee of the sick person is more open than that of the healthy one, and the sick person cannot double their knee towards the fire; and the place that is next to the swelling from the abscess is hot, because the head of the thigh comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	 And the signs of those to whom it happens accidentally, are that these incidents are contrary to those mentioned before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	 And the signs of those to whom it happens in front, are that they stretch their leg according to the accomplishment; however, do not double the knee without pain, and if one wants to make it walk, it cannot go forward, and retains its urine, and swells the ankle, and when walking, it passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	 And the signs of those to whom it happens behind, are that they cannot stretch their knee, or double it, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the hipbone is in the place below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	 The returns of this appearance of dislocation are such that you must consider if the dislocation is old, and it remains according to its disposition, then there is no remedy; and it is not necessary for him to have presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	 And in the case where the dislocation is fresh, and this is of four kinds of dislocation, then you must hasten to turn the joint, and move it inside and out, and move it to the right and left; perhaps it will return, and no other treatment is necessary.
